The Birth of the New Fascist Cabinet in Germany (Continued)

(German Correspondence) Huang Gongan

The Direction of Political Affairs of the New Schleicher Cabinet

(I) Repeated Dissolutions of Parliament

After Schleicher was officially appointed as Chancellor on the 30th, he convened the first cabinet meeting on the 31st and decided on the new direction of his political affairs. The so-called realization of the "Third Reich" policy was thus produced. Subsequently, at Schleicher's proposal, stating that the parliament could not form an absolute majority faction for the government, he requested President Hindenburg, based on Article 25 of the constitution, to repeatedly order dissolutions and restructure the parliament. This proposal was passed unconditionally. Thereupon, on February 1st, Hindenburg, based on the provisions of Article 25 of the constitution, repeatedly ordered the dissolution of the parliament, which is the representative of parliamentary democracy, by issuing so-called emergency decrees. This was another unfortunate blow. At the same time, it also indicated the decline of modern German parliamentarianism. However, Schleicher's extreme and radical political means are evident here.

(II) Implementation of Two Four-Year Plans

After the current Schleicher cabinet came to power, in addition to repeatedly ordering the dissolution of parliament and making active and drastic changes in politics, the implementation of the so-called two four-year plans is most noteworthy. The first four-year plan aims to completely liberate German farmers from their suffering. The second four-year plan is dedicated to tackling the German unemployment problem. By combining these eight years, it should be possible to restore Germany's pre-war (i.e., 1914) social and economic prosperity and its free and equal international status.

(III) Consolidating the Hindenburg Front

Consolidating the Hindenburg Front is also the new slogan of the current new cabinet. The meaning of this new slogan is generally understood to be that Germany is currently in a state of disarray, riddled with holes, and struggling under the chaotic political situation of partisan infighting. Like a group of dragons without a head, lacking a political figure as a common center of trust, this gloomy phenomenon will indeed lead Germany to some unknown misfortune. Schleicher himself used to advocate personal dictatorship, but now, due to the circumstances of the nation, he has had to abandon his prejudices and form a cabinet with Papen and others. Schleicher now believes that it is especially necessary for the whole country to unite in confidence and form the Hindenburg Front, with everyone under the leadership and banner of Hindenburg, in order to avoid division and unnecessary party strife and to save the country from its crisis.

(IV) Implementing a National Labor Service Obligation System

Since Germany's defeat in World War I in 1918, it has been restricted by the Treaty of Versailles from implementing a compulsory militarist system (i.e., all young people in the country who reach the age of eighteen must join the national army as conscripts for two years). In recent years, Germany has creatively implemented a so-called national labor service obligation system. Unemployed young people in Germany, especially unemployed university students, can freely join national social construction labor groups (such as groups for opening and building national highways, new canals, mining, and building houses). They work, enjoying the state's provision of food, clothing, and shelter, without monetary compensation. They work four hours a day and receive four hours of military physical training, completely forming a barrack-like military service life. However, in name, it is beautifully called a national labor service obligation system, in order to avoid interference from the Allied powers. (This so-called national labor service obligation system was first implemented in Hungary, then in Austria, and is now being implemented in Germany.) Its purpose is, on the one hand, to relieve unemployed workers, which is the so-called "work-for-relief" idea, and on the other hand, in addition to their work, each person must also receive four hours of military physical training. Once the country is in trouble, they can immediately become strong warriors to defend the country. This is truly a win-win situation and can be said to be a new creation in modern national policy. Especially in China's current society, it is extremely necessary to emulate this system in Germany and Austria in order to save the country from its current crisis and to promote the realization of social construction. I hereby add a few words, hoping that the people of the whole country will pay attention. Since Germany implemented this so-called "engineer-soldier system" the year before last, about 250,000 unemployed university students and other unemployed middle school youths across the country have freely joined the workforce. (I have a German classmate from university who is also a member of this team, and I often have face-to-face discussions about the experience of this life, which is extremely interesting. When I have time in the future, I will write another article to inform my countrymen.) Now, the new cabinet has specifically stated that it will make the greatest efforts to promote, encourage, protect, and maintain this national social labor service obligation system, so that it can achieve a better and more improved youth organization in the future and expand its numbers to 500,000 or 1 million people.

(V) Strictly Preventing Leftward Leaning

After the new cabinet was established, journalists from across Germany went to meet with the Minister of the Interior to inquire about his views on domestic policy. How the cabinet would deal with the left-leaning attitude was of particular interest to the journalists at that time. Minister of the Interior Dr. Frick expressed his determination to strictly prevent left-wing reactionaries in his reply to the journalists, which was very clear and resolute. Frick said that if the Communist Party does not heed the cabinet's warnings and stop its propaganda of provocation and central general strikes, the government will respond with the greatest strength and the most severe steps and methods. If the strength of the Berlin police is insufficient to fully resist the riots of left-leaning workers, in the future, members of the German Steel Helmet organization will be incorporated to assist the police in jointly protecting the security of Berlin. This plan will certainly deal a great blow and threat to left-wing activities.

(VI) Changing the Parliamentary Election Law

In order to obtain a majority of seats in the government in the future parliamentary elections, the new cabinet intends to change the parliamentary election law. German people residing in foreign countries will also have the right to vote in the future, and the number of people elected in other local areas will also be increased.

Predictions on the Future of the New Cabinet

Every time there is a change of cabinet in Germany, there are more pleasing and grand official statements of political programs. In recent years, since the invention and widespread use of the phonograph, there have also been so-called government phonograph speeches, new slogans, and emergency decrees. The former is the government's announcement of new political opinions, such as vowing to actively pursue the realization of a certain plan with the greatest determination and the greatest effort, or saying that the government has considerable confidence, etc. In short, they all say things that can give the people pleasant listening and exciting comfort. The latter is the cabinet's weapon to eliminate past bad deeds and potential forces, or other obstacles and political enemies. We in Germany have long been accustomed to these dual-track political means. In fact, although the political program sounds beautiful and the parliament has been dissolved, the new terms of the two four-year plans also shine brightly after the Russian five-year plan. In the end, whether various new attempts and new wishes can go smoothly and be safely realized and successful as Schleicher expects is a matter of great doubt, considering Germany's current internal and external environment. Just take the unemployment problem as an example. Schleicher wants to completely relieve the suffering of unemployment with a four-year plan, which I am afraid will not be easy to do. It must be known that the root of the economic panic is not only lurking in Germany itself, but is also seriously and greatly affected by the outside world. Even if Schleicher can use coercive economic policies to give some people job positions, the closure of foreign markets and the inability to distribute products abroad are beyond Schleicher's power. If products cannot be sold, factories will certainly be difficult to survive and maintain. Factory closures and the emergence of the unemployment problem are a natural result that is difficult to avoid. Whether overly ruthless means of preventing leftward leaning can prevent a large number of proletarians from making major resistance or can further intensify the struggle between the sharp left and right extremes, its future is difficult to make people optimistic. Once Schleicher's policy of preventing the left is misapplied, it will be able to help promote the growth of left-leaning forces. If so, it will cultivate Schleicher's future strong enemy and future trouble, which is by no means absolutely impossible. Let us take the previous Schleicher cabinet as an example. When he came to power, he did not seem to have everything under control, and his phonograph speeches to the people of the whole country were no less inferior to Schleicher's. Who would have thought that the unexpected would come and that everything would be beyond Schleicher's expectations? He was in power for less than eight weeks, only 54 days of short life. Once the cabinet was overthrown, where was the achievement? This is because there are often contradictions between the proposition and the environment. Moreover, the current economic panic in Germany has reached its peak. Six million unemployed workers are clamoring for food. Most of the production factories across the country have closed down completely. Credit often starts to shake. The war debt has not been fundamentally resolved. As soon as Schleicher came to power, the threat of a nationwide general strike was like a raging storm. The national finances are tight. The previous year's budget was not enough to be remedied. Tax revenues are also decreasing day by day. (In 1929, the national tax revenue was 600 million marks. In 1932, it was only

Page 8

300 million marks.) In addition, Hugenberg has always advocated capitalism, with the protection of large landowners and capitalists as his duty, but Schleicher has the color of national socialism. Although his fascist party's political program in principle recognizes the economic autonomy of private property with free activities, in practice, the demands of the fascist party do not allow large capitalists to manipulate the forces of social economy, and it advocates confiscating the property of Jews and liquidating all serfdom. Finally, Hugenberg advocates that more cities should benefit industrial groups, while Schleicher advocates that more cities should benefit the middle class and farmers. As for Papen's policies, of course, he is unwilling to leave the gentry class. Speaking of these deformed phenomena of sleeping in the same bed but dreaming different dreams, whether snakes and tigers can conspire together is very doubtful. In short, the difficulties faced by Schleicher's new cabinet, the mission entrusted to it by the country, and the urgency of the masses' desire for safety are more difficult and heavier than any previous cabinet. It can be said to be in a very serious era. Although Schleicher has extraordinary wrist strength, it is difficult to overcome this extraordinary difficulty. However, the big mystery that is not easy to solve is the repeated elections of the parliament on March 5. Schleicher believes that this parliamentary election has the power of the government as its backing and the use of political power. For the future election campaign, he can manipulate everything and increase the number of voters for his party, so he can expect the parliament to form a majority faction for the government in the future. The Communist Party will be subject to the government's strict and harsh sanctions and restraints, so that the number of voters will not decrease and the left wing will be fatally injured. If this conspiracy can succeed, it will certainly be enough to consolidate the cabinet's position, so that Schleicher can truly implement the dictatorship of the right wing. Otherwise, if the parliament still cannot produce a majority faction for the government in the future, then the fate of the cabinet may not avoid large or small fluctuations. Its future as a disaster or a blessing is not easy to determine. However, according to my humble opinion, Schleicher is indeed the most ideal political figure in Germany in the 14 years after the war. The public admiration and support he receives in Germany is no less than that of Mussolini in Italy. As far as his party is concerned, it is also the largest political party for the Allied countries, with strong momentum and new policies. His position seems to be better than that of Schleicher and others who perform solo shows. Of course, they cannot be mentioned in the same breath. Moreover, Schleicher also has considerable prestige abroad. For Germany's liberation in the 14 years after the war and the anti-Versailles Treaty movement, he can also be said to have made great contributions. Now he has been trusted by the president and supported by the whole country to come to power and form a cabinet. No matter what, it can be predicted that Schleicher will not be able to have a possible long-term position in the future.

Conclusion

We do not care whether the fate of Schleicher's three-headed cabinet this time is a disaster or a blessing. In short, German politics is actually a state on the right path. Although the parliament has been dissolved several times in the past two years, the so-called parliamentary system of democratic politics has long lost its function and role. The parliament exists in name only, and the voice of the decline of German democratic forces is constantly filling domestic and foreign public opinion. However, because Articles 48 and 25 of the German Constitution empower the government with the full power to take emergency dictatorial measures to deal with the parliament, the dissolution of the parliament is permitted by the constitution and cannot be regarded as an unfair or violent act. Throughout the process, the spirit of the rule of law has not been violated. As for the constant production of cabinet tides, from Brüning to Papen, from Papen to Schleicher, from Schleicher to Schleicher, the political situation has changed rapidly, the political direction has often shifted, and the opinion struggle has been very intense. However, all judgments of victory and defeat in the struggle are based on national public opinion. For example, when national public opinion requested that Brüning take office to form a cabinet, Brüning could certainly respond to the order and come out. Once his policies were not working or the environment was bad and he was unable to do anything, once the public called, Brüning would immediately return the political power to the people of the country, resign and give way to the worthy. As far as Schleicher's cabinet is concerned, Schleicher took office for less than eight weeks. Once he felt that he had no control over politics, he immediately resigned and did not dare to be greedy for office and delay national affairs. In short, the shift of his politics is based on the constitution and centered on political morality and personality. Therefore, the parliament can be dissolved constantly, and the cabinet tides can occur from time to time, but social life will definitely not be harmed or victimized in any way directly. This good phenomenon of the rule of law is truly worthy of our utmost admiration and envy. Looking back at the motherland, every time there is a change in the political situation, there is more exposure to the tragic scene of internal strife and bloodshed. The shift of the government's movements is centered on force, and civil war determines whether it is possible or not. It does not know what political morality and personality are, and it has never escaped the humanity of the barbaric tribal era. Now, such as the Sichuan War and the dispute between the two Lius, who is working hard for whom? This kind of civil war, which is purely based on personal interests, is truly the only factor in the sinking and self-destruction of the Chinese nation. Looking east and west, seeing others and seeing ourselves, why is the difference between Chinese and Western political morality so great? Because of the times and the things, I can't help but add another layer of suffering from the darkness of Chinese politics. (End)

Re-Convocation of the League of Nations Special Assembly (Part 1)

Chairman Hymans' Opening Remarks: Japan Bears Sole Responsibility for the Failure of Mediation

Geneva Correspondence: The League of Nations Special Assembly, convened for the Sino-Japanese dispute, was temporarily adjourned on December 9th last year. Subsequently, the Nineteen-Member Committee engaged in mediation in accordance with Article 15, Paragraph 3 of the Covenant. However, the Japanese had no sincere intention to do so, and they took advantage of the end of the year to launch a large-scale invasion of Jehol. Although there was a long period of negotiation and compromise, there was no effect in the end. Therefore, it was necessary to draft a report in accordance with Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant. After the report was drafted, the Special Assembly was reconvened on February 21st to report the failure of the mediation. At 3:30 p.m. that day, it was still chaired by Belgian Foreign Minister Hymans. The gallery was full, as the masses' psychology was eager to hear the wild theories of Japanese representative Yosuke Matsuoka. However, who knew that the meeting would be adjourned immediately after the chairman made his opening remarks, citing the need for the governments of all countries to have sufficient time to study the draft report, which would be reopened three days later? In fact, this was a pre-emptive strike, not giving the Japanese the opportunity to object before the report was discussed. The opening remarks are translated as follows:

(I have just asked you to note that the Special Assembly, at its last meeting on December 9th, instructed the Nineteen-Member Committee to study the report of the Commission of Inquiry and the statements of both China and Japan, as well as the opinions expressed in the Assembly, and to draft proposals to seek a solution to the Sino-Japanese dispute, and to submit the proposals to the Assembly for consideration at the earliest possible date.

The Nineteen-Member Committee, in completing this task, has now prepared two draft proposals and one explanatory memorandum, indicating what basis the continued pursuit of a solution to this dispute should generally take. The draft proposals and explanatory memorandum are attached to pages 12 and following of the draft report. There is no need for me

to read it again.

Since the acceptance of this text, or at least two drafts, should be passed unanimously by the entire Assembly, including both China and Japan, in order to be effective, I believe that it is not necessary to submit the draft proposals to the Assembly for discussion before obtaining the acceptance of the two governments of China and Japan. The Nineteen-Member Committee also agrees with this idea.

The Nineteen-Member Committee has authorized the Secretary-General and myself to proceed with consultations with the delegations of both China and Japan. The texts were sent to the two delegations on December 15th, and the consultations began on December 17th. The Nineteen-Member Committee and its drafting committee were, of course, constantly informed of the consultations.

Both the Chinese and Japanese representatives advocated amendments to the texts, but the amendments first proposed by the Japanese delegation were extensive and of a very different nature. Therefore, it was extremely difficult for the Nineteen-Member Committee to submit draft proposals to the Assembly and to obtain the acceptance of all members of the Assembly, including both China and Japan.

However, the Nineteen-Member Committee was still willing to make efforts to proceed within the possible period, so that the two governments, especially the Japanese government, would have sufficient time to consider the issue and make new proposals. Therefore, the Nineteen-Member Committee decided to postpone the meeting on December 20th and reopen it no later than January 16th, so that the consultations between China and Japan could continue unhindered.

In early January of this year, Shanhaiguan was occupied, and Jehol, which Japan considered to be part of Manchuria, was also under attack, causing the consultation situation to suddenly appear pessimistic. When the Nineteen-Member Committee reopened on January 16th, the Japanese delegation had no new proposals, only saying that they could be submitted in 48 hours. However, the Nineteen-Member Committee still decided to wait further and was unwilling to let months of effort go down the drain.

The Japanese government's new proposals were not sent to the Committee until January 18th. However, these proposals were unacceptable not only to China but also to the Committee itself. However, the Japanese delegation, when submitting the new proposals, specifically stated that the Japanese government attached the greatest importance to the clause in the proposals opposing the participation of non-League of Nations member states in the settlement of the case. Therefore, the Nineteen-Member Committee immediately notified the Japanese delegation that if Japan's opposition was only to this point, then it was not impossible to negotiate further with both China and Japan to seek a solution. The subsequent discussions between the Nineteen-Member Committee and the Japanese delegation were also based on this.

The Japanese delegation stated on January 21st that even if the clause in the proposals inviting non-member states to participate in the settlement of the case was deleted, the Japanese government would still not be able to accept the Committee's text. When making this reply, the Japanese delegation also represented its government in submitting new proposals. However, although the Nineteen-Member Committee's question was met with a "no" from Japan, it still did not refuse to study these new proposals. At the same time, of course, it also considered the amendments of the Chinese and Japanese delegations. After studying and considering them, it was deeply aware that it was impossible to propose a solution acceptable to both parties, at least at this time. The Chinese and Japanese delegations and the Committee itself regarded the invitation of Russia and the United States to participate in the negotiations as very important and could not delete the clause simply because of Japan's request, and at the same time further amend the clauses in the draft in accordance with the opinions put forward by Japan.

Under these circumstances, the Nineteen-Member Committee, in accordance with the resolution of the Assembly of March 11, 1932, decided to begin drafting a report in accordance with Section 4 of Article 15 of the Covenant.

Pacific Conference

Discussing the Sino-Japanese Problem

Hu Shih's Speech

The Soviet Union Also Participates in Discussing New Economic Policies

If Japan Does Not Invade, the Pending Case Can Be Resolved

Beijing Correspondence: The Pacific Conference is scheduled to be held in Canada from August 14th to 28th. Chinese representatives Hu Shih, Jen Hung-chün, Chen Heng-che, Weng Wen-hao, Chang Po-ling, and Ting Wen-chiang plan to attend at that time. This conference is particularly related to the Sino-Japanese problem and international issues in the Pacific. According to Hu Shih, the tasks of this Pacific Conference are described as follows:

Purpose of the Discussion

The Pacific Conference holds a general meeting every two years to elect representatives from various countries. The Chinese representatives participating in this conference are Ting Wen-chiang, Weng Wen-hao, Tao Meng-he, Jen Hung-chün, Chen Heng-che, Chou Yi-chun, Chang Yuan-shan, Hsu Shu-hsi, Chang Po-ling, Chang Peng-chun, Ho Lien, and Hu Shih. I myself have decided to attend. The other representatives are still considering it. Whether the representatives will travel together or separately when they depart has not yet been decided. I have no proposals for this conference. The topics to be discussed were determined a year ago. The major topics to be discussed this year are: (1) the economic conditions of various countries; and (2) the diplomatic organs in the Pacific region, including the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the Nine-Power Treaty, the League of Nations, and many other topics. Experts from various countries are studying them, and the papers of the experts are in preparation. I have no papers, only attending the discussion. The Sino-Japanese problem has no discussion results, because the Pacific Conference can only discuss international issues between countries in the Pacific region and has no resolutions. The purpose of the conference is to invite experts from various countries to jointly study various non-political issues between countries in the Pacific region, to seek appropriate solutions, to provide facts, and to hope that the research on non-political issues will help to solve purely political problems. This Pacific Conference is discussing planned international political and economic issues. The Soviet Union has also elected representatives to attend, which is the first time the Soviet Union has participated in the conference, and it is expected to be of particular interest at that time, because the Soviet Union's five-year plan has been successful, and its planned economic policies are worthy of attention and of course have discussion value.

Resolving the Sino-Japanese Problem

Regarding the Sino-Japanese problem, since the Northeast Incident occurred, not only have Japanese troops occupied the entirety of the three Northeastern provinces and created puppet regimes, but they have also invaded the entire province of Jehol. However, we must ask the Japanese: (Have the Chinese submitted? Has there been any progress in resolving the Sino-Japanese problem? Has the international relationship between China and Japan drawn even an inch closer?) A certain Japanese scholar has stated, "Absolutely not!" Even if Japanese violence advances further, even thousands of steps, and within six months or a year, they invade the entirety of North China, push to the entire coastline, and even penetrate deep into the interior of the Yangtze River basin, we can still assert that the Chinese nation will not submit. The Chinese nation's anti-Japanese and animosity towards Japan will only deepen day by day, reaching new heights daily. Resolving the Sino-Japanese problem will only become more and more distant. Even if the day comes when China's (18th and 19th-century armies) are truly completely destroyed by Japan's modern weaponry to the point of being unable to form an army, and even if the Chinese government is forced to accept a humiliating treaty of surrender, we can still assert that this will only be a temporary submission of the Chinese people's flesh and blood. It will not diminish the Chinese people's anti-Japanese sentiment in the slightest, nor will it improve the relationship between China and Japan by even an inch. Because the Chinese national spirit, under this blood baptism, will only grow stronger and stronger day by day. Or, only under this blood baptism will the Chinese nation truly and fiercely transform into Japan's permanent enemy. This is a fact that both common sense and history can guarantee. This is a fact that the Japanese people and government cannot fail to recognize. Japanese patriots and politicians should truly awaken at this time. George Bernard Shaw said to me on February 24th, "(The Japanese cannot conquer China unless they can prepare one policeman for every Chinese person. They cannot conquer China.)" (Mr. Shaw also stated this exact phrase to Japanese reporters in Tokyo a few days ago.) I replied, "(Yes, Japan cannot conquer China through violence. Japan only has one way to conquer China, which is to rein in their horses at the precipice, completely stop invading China, and instead conquer the hearts of the Chinese people.)" This is not an echo of Mr. Shaw's comments. This is my repeated and sincere advice to Japanese friends, and it is also what I want to restate as advice to the Japanese people. Japan can best learn from Germany's policies. I hope that Germany's good students have not forgotten the two historically instructive stories from the era of the German Empire's creation. On June 12, 1866, Prussia declared war on Austria. Within three weeks, the Austrian army was greatly defeated and unable to recover. After Prussia's complete victory, Bismarck advocated for an immediate ceasefire and peace negotiation, ultimately accepting a peace treaty with (no land cession and no indemnity). Bismarck's policy left Austria as Prussia's friendly nation and future ally. Four years later, Prussia went to war with France. Within seven weeks, France was greatly defeated, the French emperor was captured, and Paris was besieged. As a result of the war, France paid an indemnity of 5 billion francs and ceded two provinces. However, this great victory sowed the seeds of an irreconcilable feud between France and Germany for 48 years, leading to the Great War of 1914 and Germany's unprecedented humiliation and suffering in the last 15 years. The lessons of these two stories are worthy of consideration by the entire Japanese nation. The hatred caused by the Japanese warlords' atrocities in China has become quite difficult to eliminate today. But this is when this hatred is at its fiercest and deepest, or when a psychological shift is most likely to occur. "Nine generations of enmity, a hundred years of friendship" all hinge on whether one is aware or unaware. Japanese liberals have boldly declared, "(Japan only needs to stop invading China, and that will be enough.)" We can also respond to Japanese liberals, "(The only way for the Japanese to conquer China is to thoroughly repent for invading China.)" (18th)

Tan Ying Initiates Another Appeal

Wuxi

Price Reduction Wave in the Silk and Cloth Industry

Daxin Silk and Cloth Store, newly opened at Temple Lane Mouth in the city on the 12th of this month, published advertisements and distributed leaflets in advance, promoting price reductions. Various silk and cloth stores in the county, also in order to attract customers, specially reduced prices on their merchandise before Daxin's opening, offering discounts of 10% or 20%, and even selling sacrifice goods at 60% or 75% off. This caused a sensation throughout the county, and business was booming. On Daxin's side, facing competition from other businesses even before its opening, a banquet was held in the industry association to entertain the leaders of other businesses, requesting them to shorten the period of price reductions and raise prices. Everyone present agreed. However, after returning to their stores, a certain Mr. Jia, the top leader among the businesses, suddenly went back on his agreement and continued to offer special price reductions. This was discovered by all the other businesses, who immediately reduced their prices as well, uniformly lowering prices and using all sorts of promotional methods to attract customers. As a result, the doors of various silk and cloth stores were crowded, with business booming. The sacrifice goods were especially popular, and there were many customers eager to find bargains. Yesterday, the Tongyun Road Cloth Factory wholesale store also sold cheap remnants of cloth, causing a sensation with thousands of customers from the city and countryside. It almost became a riot, but fortunately, persuasion was effective, and no accidents occurred.

Changzhou

Merchant Shipping Vessel Robbed En Route

The Changyi night shift Junlong vessel of the Wuyi Merchant Shipping Bureau, towing the Shunli tugboat, while sailing past the Camel Bridge east of the Zhaiqiao in the Eighth District, about five li away, the previous evening, suddenly heard gunshots, and someone shouted from the north bank. Five or six armed bandits boarded the vessel, while more than ten others on the west bank crossed to the Shunli tugboat in a small boat. Entering the cabin, they searched and robbed each passenger one by one, then entered the accounting room and the rear cabin, looting everything. Suddenly, alarms were heard nearby, and the bandits fled.

Police Officer Induces Abduction of Young Girl Case

Guo Zheng, a woman from Baoying, has a son and a daughter. Her son earns a living pulling a rickshaw in the town, and her daughter is also married to a rickshaw puller. Unexpectedly, on the 19th of this month, the daughter suddenly ran away in secret. The woman searched everywhere but could not find her, and was extremely anxious. Wang Shengtang, a police officer from the Second Squad, often visited her home, and she suspected that Wang was involved in inducing the abduction. A few days ago, she brought Wang to the Third Precinct. Officer Ding interrogated him and sent him to the General Bureau, where Section Chief Dai opened a court hearing. According to Guo Zheng's testimony, she is 58 years old and from Baoying. Wang Shengtang often came to my house and said that it was a pity that my daughter was married to a rickshaw puller. Later, he also instigated my daughter on the road, and my daughter gradually showed signs of disregard. She disappeared the next day, so I brought Wang in for questioning. According to Wang Shengtang's testimony, he is 28 years old and from Hunan, and serves as a police officer in the Second Squad. Because her family does my laundry, I have been to her house a few times. The day before yesterday, I went to her house, and she said that her daughter had run away and asked me to inquire. Later, she came to the squad to find me and was scolded away by a colleague. I saw that she was worried and comforted her. I really don't know the circumstances of her daughter's escape. After hearing the testimonies, Section Chief Dai, seeing that both sides had different stories, sent both parties to the court yesterday afternoon for further investigation.

Huzhou

Child Crushed to Death by Car

Fang Baoxing, a resident of Ping'an Lane in the city's West Gate, is 40 years old and works at the Dalun Shoe Store. His wife, surnamed Mou, has a son named Laide, who is 13 years old. Yesterday afternoon, he went out to play with several classmates outside the South Gate. While walking past the Yangqiao pier near the Huzhou Station, a No. 616 empty freight car on the Beijing-Hangzhou Highway came head-on. Seeing the car, Laide panicked and ran, causing him to be hit by the car. The wheels ran over the child's body, injuring the back of his head, his waist, and his back. Upon hearing the news, the Huzhou Station detained the driver, Yu Xixiang, and handed him over to the Public Security Ninth Sub-bureau for custody. At the same time, they sent personnel to carry Laide to the nearby Gospel Hospital for treatment. After examination by the hospital doctor, it was determined that the injuries were too severe to be treated, and they instructed him to be carried back home. He died before arriving. Fang Baoxing and his wife cried bitterly upon seeing their son's tragic death. Baoxing reported the incident to the court for investigation.

City General Labor Union Telegraph

Requesting Chiang Kai-shek to be Appointed Commander-in-Chief

Ordering Frontline Soldiers not to Retreat

The City General Labor Union sent two important telegrams yesterday, recorded below.

Telegram Presented to the Central Government

Respectfully presented to the Executive Committee of the Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing. Unfortunately for the nation, externally, there are rampant foreign invaders, and internally, there are disturbances by red bandits. The nation's lifeline is hanging by a thread, and the situation is as precarious as a pile of eggs. At this time of increasing difficulty and pressing calamity, if we want to resist strong enemies and eliminate the red atmosphere, it will not be possible without gathering the nation's military forces. Although Chairman Chiang has been entrusted with important military authority, it is limited by the military commission system, which prevents the centralization of power and makes unified command difficult. Now that the flames of the invaders are burning brighter and pressing us more and more, the entire country has fallen into a state of emergency. We request that the committee immediately decide to grant Chairman Chiang the position of Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, so that military power can be unified and dispatching can be facilitated. The future of resistance against Japan deeply depends on this. This telegram is submitted with utmost urgency. The Shanghai City General Labor Union respectfully kowtows and stamps.

Telegram to Chairman Chiang

Respectfully presented to Chairman Chiang in Baoding. Recently, in the Battle of Rehe, the traitor Tang Yulin abandoned the city and fled without even seeing the enemy's shadow, causing the vast province of Rehe to fall into enemy hands in less than two weeks. This has brought shame to the nation and ridicule from foreign countries. The pain of this matter is beyond words. Protecting the nation and defending against violence is the great duty of a soldier. Even if ammunition is exhausted and reinforcements are cut off, they should continue to fight with their flesh and blood. How can they shrink back from battle or even retreat without a fight? Now that the violent Japanese are exerting all their strength to continue their advance, the survival of the nation is at stake. We hope that you will issue an order to all frontline soldiers as soon as possible, instructing them to only advance and not retreat during combat. Even if there are major sacrifices, they should not be spared. This will revitalize our national spirit and fight for our national dignity. Our people in the rear will do our utmost to provide the frontline soldiers resisting the Japanese with full support. This telegram is respectfully delivered, and we humbly request your review. The Shanghai City General Labor Union respectfully kowtows and stamps.

Expiration and Abolition of Tariff Reciprocity Agreement

Japanese Side Seemingly Expresses Agreement China Disregards Renewal, and the Other Side Has No Right to Compel

According to Xinsheng News Agency, a spokesman for the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai stated to a Xinsheng News Agency reporter yesterday that the Japanese side had agreed to abolish Parts A and B of the annex to the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement, which expires on May 15 (i.e., the provisions for reciprocity). Since China is unwilling to renew the agreement, the Japanese side has no right to compel it. However, the text of the agreement is unrelated to the abolition of Parts A and B of the annex. According to an interpretation by diplomatic circles, the abolition of the reciprocal part of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement is indeed unrelated to the text of the agreement. The newspaper's reports and the demands of various circles to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs seem to have a similar lack of clarity regarding its contents. The text of the agreement consists of five articles. Articles 1, 2, and 3 state that it is entirely about tariff autonomy, mutual equal treatment, and that the treatment of ships should not be inferior to that of other countries. Articles 4 and 5 concern the standard of language used in the agreement and its duration. There is no expiration date mentioned, and it is unrelated to the abolition of the reciprocal goods section. What is stipulated in the annex to the agreement is divided into Parts A and B. Part A contains four items: cotton goods, fish and seafood products, flour, and miscellaneous goods, which are imported into China from Japan and are granted reciprocal treatment. Except for item 4, which stipulated a one-year term and was abolished on May 15, 1931, the remaining items 1, 2, and 3 will be abolished on May 15 of this year, together with the three items in Part B. Part B concerns Chinese goods exported to Japan, which are granted reciprocal treatment by Japan. This part only includes ramie cloth, silk, and embroidered goods, and there is no item 4 that maintains a one-year term. Moreover, the names of the items listed are not as numerous as those in Part A. Abolition is advantageous to our side. As for the expiration date, rumors of May 6 or May 16 are incorrect. It is actually May 15. The signing date of the agreement was May 6, and it stipulated that it would take effect ten days from the date of signing. Therefore, May 16 is the date the agreement took effect, and May 15 is the exact date of expiration.

Letter Sent to the Taxpayer Association

转各报馆转全国同胞公鉴 (转各报馆转全国同胞公鉴 - duplicated in original) Transfer to the entire country's compatriots to know that the Japanese invaders are gaining ground and the province of East is conquered. Organizing Defense Corps

The association submitted the following to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday: Respectfully submitted, organizing a defense corps (now renamed a team) is stipulated by national government laws and regulations and is mandatory. Inland provinces and counties have already implemented it. Shanghai is our country's economic center and cultural hub. It seems inappropriate not to implement it here. Moreover, after the January 28th incident when the Japanese invaders disturbed Shanghai, the necessity of establishing a defense corps became even more apparent. Shanghai has a total population of 3.5 million. If we calculate 1/10 of it, there would be approximately 350,000 corps members who should serve. Dividing them into five years of training, there would be 70,000 people each year. If Shanghai has 30,000 active-duty soldiers and 350,000 people receive military training, they can assist the military in peacetime and serve as reserves for the national army in wartime. This is cost-effective and highly effective, fulfilling national laws and regulations while increasing local strength. It is truly a win-win situation. Now that this association's representative conference has resolved to submit a request to organize it, we hereby respectfully submit this letter for your review and approval, as it is for the public good. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Requesting Reduction of Electricity Fees

The association sent a letter to the Shanghai Concession Ratepayers Association yesterday: We are writing to inform you that, starting from January 1 of last year, the Shanghai Power Company requested the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession to approve a price increase, citing high coal prices. Now, coal prices have fallen, and the company is also using East China coal, and the East Exchange rate has fallen significantly compared to before. The cost of coal is much lower than when prices were raised. However, the company is not reducing electricity fees as a result, which shows that it is prioritizing private interests over public interests. The Municipal Council is not correcting this, which is very confusing. We are hereby writing to your association, based on the resolution of this association's representative conference, requesting you to send a letter to the Municipal Council, exercising the powers of an impartial body to uphold the principle of fairness.

Protesting Water Prices

The association sent a letter to the Concession Ratepayers Association yesterday: We are writing to inform you that water is indispensable to citizens' daily lives. Therefore, municipal authorities in civilized countries attach great importance to water supply, seeking cleanliness, low prices, and sufficiency. The Shanghai Concession's water company's charging methods were originally very reasonable, sufficiently regulating the rich and poor and adapting to prices. However, due to the Municipal Council's high-interest guarantee and the pound capital, a surcharge trend occurred. Unexpectedly, the company's greed was insatiable, and it imposed a price increase under the guise of installing meters to control waste. The Municipal Council also allowed it, and water was cut off as soon as there was any opposition, and the Municipal Council sent police to suppress it, which is a great loss to the purpose of municipal authorities. We are hereby writing to your association, based on the resolution of this representative conference, requesting you to actively oppose it and instruct the Municipal Council to quickly amend the contract to protect the interests of taxpayers. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Concession Ratepayers Association.

Second Batch of Antiquities Transported South

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday and Will Be Unloaded This Morning

Stored in the Central Bank Warehouse on Tiantang Street

The second batch of antiquities transported south from the Palace Museum in Beiping and the first batch of archives stored in Nanjing were loaded onto the Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Kuaili ship in Pukou the day before. It set sail east at 3:00 PM and docked at Jinliyuan Wharf at 1:10 PM yesterday afternoon. Because it was late, it was not transported. It was decided to start transporting it into the Central Bank warehouse for storage at 7:00 AM this morning. The details are recorded as follows.

Escorting Personnel

The people escorting the antiquities from Nanjing to Shanghai included Yu Tongkui, director of the Palace Museum, leading a staff of X people, Lu Xirong, director of the Ministry of Interior, Zhang Guoxiang, section chief, and Chen Rui, counselor, He Can, section chief, Wang Jinliang, secretary Zhai Zonghan, and Lin Qiuhai, assigned by the Executive Yuan as supervision personnel. Li Yimou and Cai Zhiang, inspectors from the Military Police Headquarters, and the Second Company of Military Police accompanied the ship for protection.

Detailed Number of Antiquities

According to Yu Tongkui, director of the Palace Museum, who spoke to a reporter from Xinsheng News Agency, there are a total of 2,554 boxes of antiquities arriving in Shanghai this time. Among them, there were 1,064 boxes from the first batch transported south, which were originally stored in the auditorium of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing. They are now being transported to Shanghai with the second batch. The second batch of antiquities transported south belonging to the Palace Museum includes 814 boxes from the Antiquities Museum, 44 boxes from the Library, and 412 boxes from the Archives Museum. The archives are also items from the Archives Museum, totaling 1,476 boxes. There are 20 boxes of miscellaneous items, totaling 1,290 boxes. Belonging to the Beiping Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior, there are 200 boxes.

Third Batch Undecided

The antiquities transported to Shanghai this time, apart from the first batch of archives transported south, are all scattered miscellaneous items. The items in the Antiquities Museum are mostly calligraphy and jade artifacts. There are also many books in the Library, which are not like the large sets of books transported south in the first instance. The total number of the first batch arriving in Shanghai was 1,054 boxes. This time there are 2,554 boxes, totaling 3,608 boxes. As to whether there will be a third transport south, it depends on the situation and the orders of the Executive Yuan.

Wharf Security

The Kuaili ship docked at Jinliyuan Wharf at 2:10 PM. The French Concession Police Department sent more than 30 Chinese and foreign detectives to the scene to stand guard. The Bund road along the Kuaili ship was cordoned off with hemp ropes at both ends to cut off traffic. All of the lighters were also filled with detectives. At 3:00 PM, it was decided to start transporting the goods today, so part of them were withdrawn, leaving three people standing guard on the road and five people (three Chinese and two Westerners) patrolling the lighter. The Municipal Public Security Bureau's water patrol team was on guard outside the ship.

Storing This Morning

Because the time was too late yesterday, it was feared that it would not be possible to transport all of them ashore, so they were not transported. Starting at 7:00 AM this morning, the transport will begin, still handled by the Maotai Company, using more than a dozen cars to transport them back and forth to the Central Bank warehouse at No. 26 Tiantang Street for storage. The French Concession Police Department will send one patrolman and one detective to protect each car. (Xinsheng News Agency)

Hand Grenade Found on Foch Road the Night Before

Zhang Xueliang Suffers a False Alarm

At 7:40 PM the night before, someone threw a hand grenade next to the bamboo fence of the east gate of Zhang Xueliang's residence at No. 181 Foch Road in the French Concession. The grenade landed in the gap at the kitchen doorway and exploded with a loud noise, shaking the roof tiles. Zhang was sitting idle in the new building when he suddenly heard the loud noise and ordered someone to investigate. At first, those around him suspected that it was a car tire exploding, but the chef reported that the loud noise came from nearby and that there was a strong smell of gunpowder. As a result, a hand grenade shell was found next to the icebox on the left side of the house, with a small, broken stool nearby and two wooden sticks in the center blown to pieces. After confirming, the detectives sent by the French Concession Police Department for protection immediately reported to the police department by phone. Deputy Commissioner of Police Raubert, Political Director Serre, and many detectives rushed to inspect the scene, picked up the damaged grenade shell, and took it back for filing and investigation. At the same time, the Public Concession also sent many Chinese and Western detectives to the border to take a look. Before long, those who heard the news and rushed to express their condolences arrived one after another.

Anhui Prisoners Save Food to Aid the Volunteer Army

Inmates Zhu Liyan, Chen Jinglu, Wang Linchuan, Chen Huizhi, and others, 151 male prisoners and Zhao Zhou's, Fan Liang's, and others, 19 female prisoners in the West Prison of Sixian County, Anhui Province, collectively reduced their food rations for three days and accumulated 10 yuan in foreign currency to aid the volunteer army. They jointly sent a letter to the Shanghai Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association, stating: We are prisoners in prison, but we are fortunate to receive rations from the country. Last autumn, when Prison Officer He Guan took office, he saw that the prisoners' rations were purchased and eaten on their own, and they were not able to satisfy their hunger. Therefore, he urgently sought ways to help, first establishing a cooking area and then creating a factory for weaving cloth. As we prisoners were working diligently in prison, we suddenly heard that the Japanese pirates had invaded our eastern lands in the September 18th Incident last year. Fortunately, our country's volunteer army vowed to kill the enemy, and we also received donations from all over the country. Upon hearing this, we were all moved to tears. Alas, we prisoners are sons of the Yellow Emperor, originating from the Central Plains, and we regret being trapped in prison, unable to jump out and kill the enemy. Now, we prisoners are willing to reduce our food rations for three days and contribute 10 yuan in foreign currency to help the volunteer army kill the enemy. We respectfully request the prison officials to allow us to send the funds to Shanghai and humbly ask you not to disdain our meager contribution. We also hope that the newspapers will inform all prisoners in prisons across the country to work diligently. If prisoners are useful in fighting the enemy, we are willing to use our flesh and blood to block the enemy's advance. If we can annihilate all the enemies in one fell swoop, it will be a great honor for our country. Otherwise, our spirits will forever guard the border and defend our country.

Dangerous Situation of the Songkou Seawall

Damaged by Tides for Days

Jin County Magistrate Requests Funds for Emergency Repairs

Due to the recent hurricanes in Wusongkou, the seawall in the area north of the Lion Grove Rock Cave has been eroded by the wind and tides and is gradually collapsing, creating a dangerous situation. Jin Jinqingzhang, the magistrate of Baoshan County, convened a meeting of various agencies to discuss the matter. As a result, 195 zhang of the northern section of the Yanchi segment of the Beishidong project and 60 zhang of the main project of the Zhangjiazhaid seawall are considered to be in critical condition and urgently need repair. It was resolved to submit a request to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, instructing the Construction Department to allocate the remaining 21,000 yuan from the emergency repairs in the 20th year of the Republic to meet the urgent need.

Reporting the Purpose

Chairman Wang Xiaolai reported: Since the government decided to cancel China's participation in the Chicago Exposition due to urgent military needs and financial difficulties, we deeply understand the government's extraordinary measures. However, considering the international perspective and economic difficulties, we have jointly agreed to participate automatically under the name of the Republic of China's Chicago Exposition Exhibitor Association, under the guidance and assistance of the government. We have also formulated articles of association, drafted participation procedures, and concrete measures, and submitted them to the Ministry of Industry for record and to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for review. We have also forwarded them to the U.S. Minister in China for review and telegraphed the Consul General in Chicago to provide guidance for our participation in the United States to facilitate the process. We have limited capabilities and a heavy responsibility. Fortunately, since the establishment of our association, we have received support and assistance from various circles, and the scale has been roughly established. However, international activities require collective efforts to be effective. Now, to seek assistance and guidance, we are briefly reporting the preliminary plans, preparations, and general budget: 1. This association will use basic exhibits such as lacquerware, porcelain, pottery, silk, embroidery, jade, carpets, summer cloth, tea, carvings, and art as the basis for its structure. 2. All expenses for exhibits should be coordinated and prepaid by the association as a whole, regardless of territorial divisions. The total amount required is 150,000 yuan in foreign currency. A special economic committee will be formed under this association to handle economic matters. A summary of the budget is listed separately. (3) In addition to the exhibits collected by this association, other exhibits or books and brochures submitted by the government or groups of manufacturers for participation and that do not affect the budget of this association will be transported to the United States for display by this association. (4) All exhibits should be shipped to the United States by the end of the month. (5) For the convenience of carrying out the association's affairs, Zhang Xianglin, the director of the preparatory committee's office, should be hired by this association to travel to the United States to assist in all matters. (6) This association should request the government to telegraph Minister Shi to personally attend the opening ceremony of the Chinese pavilion at the Chicago Exposition. (7) When members of this association travel abroad, they must inspect themselves and their belongings to avoid problems. (6) Standards for the construction of the special pavilion and its budget: (A) The architectural plan was drafted by the American architectural expert Murphy. (B) The architectural form is a city wall and drum tower, or a surrounding wall with exhibition rooms built inside, and a garden in the center. (C) The building

will occupy a portion of the original site of the government pavilion, with an area of approximately 38,400 square feet (at least 20,000 square feet). Construction can begin as soon as the government formally notifies us. The preliminary participation plan of this association is roughly as described above. However, we have recently received a telegram from the Chicago Exposition Authority through US Counselor Anno: (1) The architectural cost estimated by Murphy, which we requested, is considered insufficient. (2) The meeting period is urgent, and we are concerned that the construction cannot be completed as scheduled. After discussion, this association intends to slightly change the construction standards to fit the budget. However, this is just a proposal based on the current situation of this association. If we can expand the organization, it will be easy to remedy. As for the construction deadline, if funding is not a problem, there will be no problem in reality. This is our humble opinion, and we hope to receive your enlightenment.

Achievements of the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau in Dredging the Songjiang

The Shallow Shoal of Yujidun Has Also Been Dredged Deeper

The Zi Lin Bao reports: Since the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau was entrusted by the Municipal Government to deepen and widen the Suzhou Creek, the downstream navigation channel has greatly improved. The previously narrow and silted riverbed can now accommodate ships with a draft of five feet for three miles upstream from the confluence of the Suzhou Creek and the Huangpu River. After four more years of work, this depth can be maintained for thirteen miles above the confluence. According to the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau, since being entrusted to dredge the river, the specified depth is at least five feet below the low water line, and the width is at least seventy-five feet. Construction began on February 11th of the 20th year of the Republic. By the end of February of this year, 625,000 cubic feet of silt, or approximately 700,000 tons, had been excavated. The dredging has now reached the vicinity of Binlang Road, and the shallow shoal of Yujidun, which is an obstacle to navigation thirteen miles upstream, has also been dredged deeper. It is understood that the river extends for thirteen and a half miles within the jurisdiction of Shanghai and is scheduled to be dredged for six years. Currently, there are four dredgers, two tugboats, and five barges operating to transport the mud. Sometimes, cranes or divers are used to remove stones and other heavy objects. The engineering personnel of the bureau also go to supervise the work from time to time.

Japanese Warships Measure the Depth of Our Waterways

Yesterday afternoon, rumors of an alert in Tianjin and Dagukou spread in Shanghai. Because a ship was scheduled to sail to Tianjin today, various shipping companies in the city telegraphed Tianjin to inquire, but no reply had been received by the evening. Yesterday, a passenger from Tianjin and the owner of a Chinese shipping company told reporters that when their ships left Tianjin and Dagukou, the situation in Tianjin was quite calm. However, about thirteen miles from the Dagukou, four Japanese destroyers and one cruiser were seen. As they passed by, the Japanese warships were sending their naval surveying team, led by officers, to measure the depth of the water along the Dagukou and Baihe River by means of small boats, and they were secretly marking shallower areas. Otherwise, nothing else was seen. Yesterday, when the ships arrived in Shanghai and passed outside the Wusongkou, the Japanese flagship Izumo, which was conducting target practice and firing cannons outside Flower Island, was seen returning to Shanghai. The Japanese warship proceeded first, and about three miles outside of Baolonggang, the warship also sent a surveying team to measure the depth of the water along the Pudong coast.

30,000 Yuan to be Issued Next Week

Disaster Victims Petitioned the War Zone Authorities Yesterday

The United Association of Disaster Victims in Zhabei stated that after receiving housing loans last year, they immediately began construction. Therefore, yesterday, they sent representatives Shen Wenbin and three others to petition the Shanghai War Zone Relief Committee, requesting the immediate allocation of the 30,000 yuan relief fund due from the Shanghai North Charity Race to enable early completion. They also requested the early distribution of loans to the second batch of disaster victims (who have not yet received any funds). Seamen's New Trend

Seamen Oppose Registration

Shanghai seamen, due to the Ministry of Communications' promulgation of regulations for managing seamen, stipulating that all seamen from shipowners down, regardless of appointment, promotion, transfer, employment, or dismissal, must obtain a handbook from the Navigation Administration Bureau, paying a fee of two to five yuan each time, totaling nine items. The seamen unanimously opposed the registration fee. As a result, the Ministry agreed to cancel the registration fees for suspension and dismissal. The seamen believe that with seven types of registration fees still remaining, requiring fees for every action of seamen, which is unprecedented in other countries, merely canceling two types is not a thorough solution. They have submitted a second petition, collectively signed, demanding the fundamental abolition of this harsh regulation as soon as possible. The petition has been drafted and sent to both the Navigation Bureau and the Ministry of Communications.

Marine Engineers Petition

Since the tragic accident of the Da Yun ship last year and the New Affairs Zhao disaster this year, the Ministry of Communications has strictly regulated the personnel in the engine departments of various ships. Only those with nautical knowledge and experience, certified by the shipping company, are allowed to serve as officers in the engine department. Qualifications are limited, and the Ministry issues qualification certificates. The procedures for obtaining the certificate are cumbersome, requiring a medical examination and a review of qualifications by the Ministry. Each certificate costs more than fifty yuan and is valid for only five years. Currently, there are nearly one hundred certified marine engineers in Shanghai without current positions. Although the Ministry of Communications has instructed various shipping bureaus not to hire marine engineers without certificates, many merchants in Shanghai are employing marine engineers without certificates, causing qualified personnel to become unemployed, making the Ministry's certificate equivalent to waste paper. Yesterday, all unemployed marine engineers decided to petition Director Zhu of the Navigation Administration Bureau this morning, requesting him to handle the matter fairly.

Water Rate Negotiations Still Unresolved

The Da Mei Wan Bao reported that the rumors of a compromise solution to the public concession's water rate dispute are inaccurate. The recent meeting of the Housing Association, where it was announced that the water rate dispute had been resolved after recent negotiations, agreeing to pay 10% of the rent before the end of February and calculating according to the water meter thereafter, also deviates from the facts. According to what this newspaper (Da Mei Wan Bao) has learned today, the two sides have not yet reached a mutually satisfactory solution. Currently, the company only promises that if the water rate is extremely high according to the water meter, the water company may grant special concessions to the owners, roughly up to 10% of the rent. However, this 10% figure is only a discretionary standard for concessions, not a formal fixed rate. This concession plan is also subject to the circumstances of each household and will be granted separately, not uniformly applied. The negotiations between the owner's association representative, Feng Bingnan, and the representatives of the Public Works Department and the water company are still ongoing, and no concrete solution has yet been found.

Hongzhen Ship Runs Aground, Causing Trouble

Damaging Thai Ship and Customs Pontoon

The Hongzhen ship of the Sanbei Company, which travels between Yichang, Shashi, Hankou, and Shanghai, encountered shallow water and a heavy load on the morning of the 18th of this month when arriving at the Gu Matou near Shashi. The ship ran aground. The shipowner tried various methods, including reversing, but was unable to escape the shallows for a full day and night. Subsequently, the Shashi branch specially hired a large tugboat to tow the Hongzhen ship with great effort. However, the Hongzhen ship was deeply embedded in the sand. It was not until the river rose greatly on the afternoon of the 19th that the tugboat pulled it out of the shallows. Unfortunately, due to excessive force, the Hongzhen ship damaged the nearby Thai ship on both sides and then crashed into the Shashi Customs pontoon, damaging it. The extent of the damage is being investigated. The Hongzhen ship itself was not damaged.

Do not Publicize Lawsuits Concerning Morality

Lawyers Association Notifies Attention

The Shanghai Lawyers Association yesterday issued a notice to all members stating: "I would like to inform you that according to the proposal of Member Yan Yinwu, regarding civil and criminal litigation cases handled by various lawyers, they often arbitrarily decorate the content, regardless of whether it concerns social morality, and compile it into a legendary news story, or publish the original lawsuit verbatim on the newspaper. Social people use it as a chat, and people without knowledge take it as a fun influence on morality, which is huge. If this is not changed for a long time, the abuse will be unbearable. You should notify all lawyers that for civil and criminal litigation cases related to morality, you must not publish the original lawsuit or related documents in the newspapers, in order to save the degeneration." The first 11222323 joint meeting of the Board of Directors and Supervisors of this Association resolved that Member Yan's proposal is related to the world, people's hearts, and lawyers' ethics, and should be communicated to all members for information and compliance. "

Detailed Report on the Severe Disaster in Shaanxi

The China Jisheng Association in this port has recently received a report from the Chang'an Branch in Shaanxi, transferred by Mr. Wang Jishi, the director of the shelter set up by the association in Wugong County, stating the details of the organization and the current situation in the disaster area. It was found that the Wugong shelter, since its opening on the 12th day of the first month of this year, first collected more than 200 people on the 3rd and 4th days, especially those who were extremely distressed. In the middle, there were frequent shortages, and many people in the cabinet. In January, a total of men and women disaster victims were collected, more than 500. Everyday, people came to the shelter to complain and ask for help, which is not recorded. It is difficult to save people universally. That is, the staff went to the mountains on February 3 to feed more than 140 people. Each disaster victim was given a set of white cloth and a dai mouth, with more than a liter of dry food stored, as needed along the way. On the 4th, another 150 disaster victims were sent, and staff were sent to be the front station to check the accommodation address for the disaster responsibility. Every day, according to the disaster victims' pace, they can only walk 40 or 50 miles, or they will not be able to handle it. Now, it is estimated that 600 to 700 people have gone to the mountains to eat because the price of grain in the mountains is slightly cheaper. The girls and children who cannot walk, about 200 people, will be kept in Wugong for adoption, and will be reconsidered after the wheat autumn. First, staff were sent to the Nanshan area to find a place where the price was relatively reduced, to transfer to eat. According to the letter, there are many people who have fled in Nanshan, which has led to rising grain prices. It is better to go to Gansu to punish the suspension, and its price is calculated in Wugong dou, each dou can be 50 or 60 jiao, which is three times less than Wugong. A shelter address has been set in Huixian, which is more than 600 miles from Wugong. Thinking that Hugong is currently not raining, the fields are red, the red sun is the sky, and the ash is shallow. Rather than waiting for death, it is better to eat and extend life. Now Wugong has collected more than 400 people, and is preparing to send them to Huixian for adoption. At this moment, the fields in Wugong have no Wangzhu, and they are used as firewood, which is very painful. Hungry bellies, day and night, are trying to find a plan. Everything is known. As for the situation of the guests in the shelter, some young people are so hungry that they are bone-thin, and children are in love with their relatives. They are fed in the shelter, and they are kind to their families. They are persuaded in every way, but they keep crying. They are allowed to see their parents. Their brother is dying because of his father. His heart is burning, and his brother is handling it. He is forcibly ordered to die. His family members stop him, send him to the temple at night, and send him home in the morning. He recounts the general situation of his parents' impending death, and sends him back to the shelter for custody. Please do not let him go. His father and brothers will also say goodbye forever. Such a situation is endless. The people in the four villages of Wugong are almost exhausted, not to mention ten rooms and ten empty rooms, no chickens and dogs are heard, the villages are cool, and thorns are everywhere. Knowing that you will be unable to cope with disaster relief, but the tragedy is so great that you dare not carelessly report it. If you are willing to add pity and give me a helping hand, Fumin will be rebuilt, etc. According to this, the association saw this tragic situation, in addition to the Wugong shelter, 5,000 yuan had been allocated for disaster relief, and the day before yesterday, 1,200 shi of rice were transported to Shaanxi to transfer Wugong for urgent relief. A drop in the bucket, saving cannot be saved. An able to get the magic of the gods, Hui Tao hungry people, so that they can linger on their last breath, to be able to rise from the dead? Looking forward to it.

Li Minghui's Love Affair Case

Murderer Wang Nengxiang Appeals

Wang Nengxiang Claims to Have Been in Guangzhou at the Time of the Incident

The Judge Believes This Point Needs Investigation

Miss Li Minghui, who gained fame for singing new songs, was in Hong Kong last spring. Due to a love triangle, her two lovers, Zheng Guoyou and Feng Deqian, suddenly turned from friends into enemies.
