Chen Kaihong

Attempted Murder of Parents

A Shocking Incident

The Elderly Father Luckily Survived

Around 10 PM the night before last, an elderly man was found collapsed outside the Dadongmen Gate in Shijia Alley, Nanshi. He had an extremely thick hemp rope around his neck and a knife wound on the back of his head, with fresh blood flowing from the wound, indicating a possible murder. The responsible police precinct was notified and sent officers to the scene. They found the elderly man lifeless, but his body was still warm. They untied the hemp rope around his neck, and the elderly man suddenly regained consciousness. He was rushed to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. According to him, his own son and daughter-in-law were plotting to kill him. The incident is truly shocking. Here are the details of the case:

Chen's Family History

Chen Qiao, a native of Yangzhou, is 58 years old. His wife, Ms. (surname), gave birth to two sons. The elder son, named Kaihong, is 33 years old and married to Yang (surname), who is 17 years old and from Baoying. The couple runs a pancake shop at No. 95, Jia Du, Pudong. The younger son, named Xiaogou, is 22 years old and works as a leather craftsman, residing at No. 42, Yangjiazhai, Pudong. Chen used to make a meager living vaccinating people in his hometown. However, with the development of hospitals in recent years, people prefer to go to hospitals for vaccinations. As a result, Chen had no one to consult and, being old, could no longer make a living. He had no choice but to come to Shanghai and live with Kaihong, relying on his son for support.

Abandoned in the Courtyard

However, his son Kaihong has a violent temper, and his daughter-in-law Yang (surname) is unkind. Seeing that Chen was not contributing to production and was living in their house, they became disgusted. Soon, they began to abuse him. In June of last year, Kaihong and his wife beat Chen severely over a minor matter. Still not satisfied, they stripped Chen naked, tied his hands and feet with rope, and abandoned him in the courtyard. At that time, Chen's back was exposed to the scorching sun, and soon his entire body blistered, causing excruciating pain. Fortunately, a passerby saw him and pleaded with Kaihong, who then released Chen. Afterward, Chen's back became severely ulcerated due to the heat, and it took a long time to heal.

A Small Test with a Kitchen Knife

Later, Kaihong went a step further and planned to murder Chen to free himself from the burden of having him in this world. One night, while Chen was fast asleep, Kaihong used a kitchen knife to strike Chen's head. Fortunately, Chen had already woken up and quickly covered his head with a quilt, avoiding a fatal blow. Chen cried out for help, but Kaihong, fearing that the neighbors would notice, did not continue the attack. Afterward, Chen was still afraid of incurring resentment from his son, so he endured it and did not publicize the matter. After a few days, Kaihong, seeing that the murder had failed, drove Chen out of the house. Chen then filed a complaint with the Shanghai District Court, accusing Kaihong of neglecting his duty to support him and of abusing him. However, he did not reveal the attempted murder. The case was heard once, and the court ruled that Kaihong should continue to provide support and pay him two jiao a day for living expenses.

Tiptoeing to Strike

Since Chen returned to his son's house, Kaihong became even more resentful. He would scold or beat Chen at the slightest offense. However, Chen, thinking of the father-son relationship, endured it silently. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, Kaihong and Yang secretly discussed murdering Chen again. Fortunately, Chen learned of the plan and, around 9 PM that evening, made an excuse to go out, crossing the river to Nanshi to discuss the matter with a friend. After Chen left, Kaihong feared that he knew their secret and would report it to the authorities. He immediately had the evil thought of going all the way. He immediately gathered his younger brother Xiaogou and his wife Yang, hiding a thick hemp rope and a sharp knife, and followed Chen to Nanshi. Waiting until he walked to a secluded place, they struck. Chen did not realize that his own son, whom he had raised, was following him, intending to take his life.

Tightly Pulling the Rope

Before long, Chen reached Shijia Alley, a secluded place. Kaihong and the others rushed forward. First, they struck the back of his head with a sharp knife. Chen cried out in pain. Before the cry finished, Kaihong and the others put a hemp rope around his head and pulled it tightly. Chen did not see who was attacking him. However, he heard his daughter-in-law Yang shouting, "Hurry up and pull!" Soon, Chen could not breathe and could not move his hands and feet. Seeing this, Kaihong and the others knew that they had achieved their goal and abandoned him on the roadside. They then crossed the river and returned home. Afterward, someone discovered an elderly man murdered in Shijia Alley and immediately reported it to the police precinct, requesting an investigation.

Regaining Consciousness

After receiving the report, Chief Yi, recognizing the seriousness of the matter, immediately ordered Police Chief Lan Yucheng to rush to Shijia Alley. They found that Chen was lifeless, but his body was still warm. They quickly untied the hemp rope around his neck and administered artificial respiration. Before long, Chen suddenly regained consciousness, moving his hands and feet. The police chief knew he could be saved and rushed him to Shanghai Hospital. Chen then tearfully recounted the events to the police chief. The police chief, amazed that such a thing could happen, took him to the precinct. The chief interrogated him. The next day, around 8 AM, he sent officers to Pudong to arrest Kaihong, Xiaogou, and Yang. During the interrogation, Kaihong and the others, realizing that their crime had been discovered unexpectedly, were terrified. However, they denied everything. They were detained temporarily. The police were sent to Pudong to investigate their neighbors. According to the neighbors, Kaihong and the others had always been disreputable. Yang was also a well-known harlot. When she worked in a factory, she had an affair with a worker. When she was 15 years old, she secretly gave birth to a child. The police reported this to Chief Yi, stating that Chen Kaihong and the others were extremely unfilial and dared to murder their parents, committing extreme lawlessness. He immediately ordered a written report to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau at around 4 PM that afternoon for strict investigation. At around 11 AM yesterday morning, Chen, who had not eaten anything all morning, felt hungry. He spent money to buy three pancakes. Just as he was about to eat, he saw his son Kaihong and the others detained in the detention center. Knowing that it was noon and they would not have lunch, he endured his hunger and sent the three pancakes to the detention center, asking his son and daughter-in-law to share them. However, Kaihong and the others shook their heads in refusal. Despite his repeated urging, they still refused to accept. He was overcome with grief, and tears welled up in his eyes. He could not swallow the pancakes he had bought, so he threw them away. Ah, the love of a calf-licking mother, how deep it is! What should those who are sons feel upon reading this article?

After arriving in Shanghai, he hid at No. 71 Xuxie Branch Road, Nanshi. He was apprehended and handed over to the First Special District Court. After repeated negotiations with British officials in Hong Kong, it was decided that the case would be handled here. Subsequently, several court hearings were held. Finally, he was sentenced to life imprisonment. The details have been recorded in previous reports. However, after receiving the sentence, Wang Nengxiang expressed dissatisfaction and submitted a petition to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, requesting an appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu of the Criminal Division, along with Assessors Zhao and Jiang, specially convened a joint court to hear the case. However, the witness Li Minghui was reportedly out of Shanghai due to other affairs and would not return until a week later. Therefore, she did not appear in court yesterday. Judge Yu ordered Wang Nengxiang to be brought to the court and asked about the reasons for his appeal. Wang claimed that the court had not provided conclusive evidence of his murder charge and that he was not convinced. He requested that Xu Rongsheng, an accomplice in the case in Hong Kong, be transferred to the court for confrontation, stating that only then would he be satisfied. Judge Yu stated that Xu Rongsheng and the others had already been questioned in detail by the Hong Kong authorities, and their statements had been copied and sent to the first instance court, so there was no need to transfer them again. He rejected Wang Nengxiang's request and continued to ask about other reasons. Wang claimed, "I went to Guangzhou on the tenth day of the second lunar month last year and left Guangdong for Hong Kong on the second day of the third lunar month. The incident happened on March 24th of the Gregorian calendar. At that time, I was still in Guangzhou. Huang Shaotang can prove this. Huang works as a carpenter at the Dadong Gramophone Company on Taiping North Road outside Guangzhou City. When I was in Guangdong, I stayed with Huang every day, so Huang certainly knows my whereabouts. This should be investigated." The court believed that this point should be investigated and ordered a re-examination. Wang Nengxiang was taken back to the police station for detention.

Robbery and Rape Case

Two Robbers Sentenced to Death

Dissatisfied with Initial Life Sentences

Appeals Result in Death Sentences

Zhao Wenbao, 27 years old, and Dong Yonghong, 25 years old, both from Gaoyou, Jiangbei, were found to have gathered accomplices and used weapons to rob Liang Xuefu, a fellow villager living in an unnumbered flat in Yangshupu Road, of property worth 211 yuan on the morning of November 23rd last year, and to have taken turns raping his 19-year-old sister Liang Xiaomei (also known as Zhou Xiaomei). The case was discovered, and the two were arrested by Chinese and foreign detectives from the Yulin Road police station and handed over to the First Special District Court, where they were each sentenced to life imprisonment. Zhao and Dong were dissatisfied and appealed. Judge Yu of the Second Branch High Court believed that the two had committed heinous crimes and changed the sentences to death, which were submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval and ordered to be carried out. At 2 PM yesterday afternoon, Execution Judge Shen Shanzeng arrived at the Third Criminal Court and ordered Zhao and Dong to be brought in for questioning about their age, origin, whether they had any last words, and to contact their families. Zhao Wenbao still claimed that he was innocent and asked his father, Zhao Zifeng, to come and collect his body. His address was a shed without a number on Yanshan Road, Yangshupu. Dong Yonghong stated that his home was at No. 34, Songmaoli, Songpan Road, his father's name was Dong Shoupeng, and he asked to be notified to collect his body. He also had two silver yuan and eight copper coins, which he asked to be handed over to him. He also claimed that he had been having an affair with Zhou Xiaomei when she was working at the Dakang Cotton Mill. Judge Shen declared that the day for execution had arrived and there was no need to say more. He ordered them to be sent to the District Court for execution. The Chinese and foreign police took the two criminals down, along with the case files and photographs, and escorted them in a car to the execution ground at the Second Prison in Caohejing. The prosecutor commissioned by the court arrived at the scene, verified the identities of the two criminals, ordered the bailiffs to bind them according to the law, and executed them by firing squad.

Generous Guests Turn into Violent Robbers

Robbery in Cian Lane

Staff of the Maoye Factory Beaten and Injured

Qian Jiachen Also Bound and Imprisoned in the Storeroom

Cian Lane on Ningbo Road is located behind the Xinxin Company on Nanjing Road. The area is densely populated and quite lively. The six buildings in the lane are all high-end commercial establishments. The Maoye Woolen Factory also has a distribution office at No. 2 in the lane, with Qian Jiachen's residence with his mistress upstairs. At 7 PM the night before last, a young man dressed in luxurious clothing entered the Maoye accounting room under the pretense of asking for the owner. Without saying a word, the factory staff mistakenly thought he was a generous guest and invited him to sit down. Then, the so-called handsome young man suddenly pulled out a pistol and pointed it at the accountant's chest, ordering him to hand over the keys. At the same time, five other men, all dressed in fashionable clothing and also carrying pistols, entered and warned them not to make a sound. They used the lead wires they had brought to tie up all thirteen Maoye staff members and push them into the storeroom. They began searching, but because no one was in charge of Maoye, they could not find the key to the safe. They beat the staff members and searched their pockets, obtaining over one hundred yuan. The robbers' courage did not falter, and they were still dissatisfied. They then rushed upstairs to Qian Jiachen's residence. Qian's room was richly decorated, but there were no readily available diamonds and jewelry. They also tied up Qian and his wife with lead wires and dragged them into the storeroom downstairs. They ransacked the boxes and chests, taking whatever they pleased. In the end, because it was inconvenient to carry, they only took several dozen yuan in cash and three pieces of beautiful qipao fabric. After things quieted down, the factory staff dared to break out of the storeroom. The distance from the police station was only a stone's throw away, yet the robbers dared to rob in broad daylight and at their leisure. The robbers' audacity was truly great. It is now heard that the residents of the lane, Shi Jiqun, Huang Yuzhai, and Chen Cunren, etc., to prevent future incidents, have already written to the Tonghe property management office to request additional armed patrol officers, and have also sent an official letter to the police department, requesting that they conduct a thorough investigation to maintain the security of the lane.

Murder of Husband by Adulterous Wife

Wife Flees, Lover Arrested

Son Kidnapped to Shanghai

Child Welfare Society Provides Shelter and Relief

The China Child Welfare Association at No. 20, Museum Road, received an orphan named Hu Jusheng, 9 years old, yesterday from the Municipal Public Security Bureau. It was learned that the child's home was in Dongfenglin, Changzhou. His father, named Ageng, made a living by farming. His mother, Zhang (surname), was unfaithful and had an affair with a local man. Their passion was extreme. Because her husband was watching her, she held a grudge in her heart. One night in June last year, Ageng was relaxing at the door, lying on a bench, when he suddenly fell asleep. The adulterous wife had the sudden intention to kill, and invited her lover to the kitchen to take a kitchen knife. While Ageng was asleep, she used the knife to slash his throat. The lover also helped to commit the crime. Instantly, blood splattered everywhere, and Ageng died tragically. They buried the body and destroyed the evidence in the middle of the night. However, they were spotted by a neighbor. The adulterous wife and lover, knowing that they could not escape punishment, set fire to the house and fled separately. It is heard that the lover was arrested and punished according to the law. Zhang (surname) disappeared without a trace, abandoning her nine-year-old child, who lost his support. He was kidnapped to Shanghai, where he was discovered by the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Child Welfare Society for shelter and education.

Xie Zhongfu and Others Feted Shao Lizhi

Shao Lizhi, Chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government, recently came to Shanghai. Mr. Shao has achieved considerable success in governing Gansu. Xie Zhongfu and his brother Xiaochu, merchants from Gansu living in Shanghai, hosted a banquet at the Bankers' Association to welcome Mr. and Mrs. Shao. Among those present were Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Chen Zhongsheng, Director of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Bureau, and Qu Wenliu. During the banquet, Mr. Shao spoke at length about the situation in Gansu Province. The guests and hosts parted in joy at 11 PM.

Kidnapping Robbers Daring to Impersonate Detectives

Even Inquiring About News at the Robbed Store

Huang Tianbo, a 31-year-old Anhui native residing at No. 12 Hefeng Lane, Roberts Road, Shanghai West, was formerly a factory worker. Recently unemployed and idle, he colluded with robbers. On the evening of the 22nd of last month, at 10 PM, he and five other accomplices at large, including Zhang Chengyou and Zhang Yuede, armed with weapons, broke into the Hengyuan cigarette and paper shop owned by Wu Youliang at No. 396 Malan Road in the French Concession, stealing tens of dollars in various currencies before fleeing. The victim reported the incident to the police station, requesting an investigation. Unexpectedly, on the 9th of this month, Huang pretended to be a detective dispatched by the police station to inquire at the victim's shop whether a robbery had occurred and the amount of silver dollars stolen. Shop assistant Mao Genxiang recognized Huang's face, immediately recalling that Huang was the thief who had been keeping watch outside the door during the robbery. Mao then followed Huang to the Ximen Road intersection, where he alerted the police, who arrested Huang and brought him to the police station. During interrogation by the police chief, Huang, due to grudges with his housemate Tao Rongquan, a Jiangbei native, and Wang Laosi, also a Jiangbei native residing at No. 18 in the same lane, implicated Tao and Wang as accomplices in the robbery. Subsequently, a detective arrested Tao and Wang for questioning. Tao and others were completely clueless. Upon further interrogation, Huang confessed to falsely accusing them out of spite. After investigation by detectives, he was escorted to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division yesterday. Judge Wang Gangxu conducted the trial. First, the police lawyer Yuan Jiahuang presented the case, stating that the police were prosecuting the first defendant under Articles 348 and 180 of the Criminal Code for robbery by a gang of three or more and false accusation. The second and third defendants were not being prosecuted. Witness Mao Genxiang testified that he saw Huang keeping watch outside during the robbery and later coming to investigate, so he followed him and alerted the police to arrest him. Huang Tianbo confessed that he went to rob with Zhang Chengyou, Zhang Yuede, and others, and was given five dollars afterwards. Initially, they told me to watch for the police while they went to get water. I didn't know they were robbing, so I went to the shop to inquire, intending to be arrested, Zhang and others against Tao and Wang

Ant Library

Open to Readers Nationwide

Book Catalog Published Simultaneously

The Ant Library was founded by the [Ant Society] for promoting cultural movements. Through painstaking efforts over the years, its collection has gradually increased, and its internal resources have been enriched. Based on the society's mission to serve the public and promote social education, it is now open unconditionally to readers nationwide, without any fees or deposits. It also adopts a fully correspondence-based borrowing and returning system, so that people in remote areas can also enjoy the benefits of borrowing books. This is unique among domestic libraries and will undoubtedly benefit culture significantly. Recently, the library's workload has become intense. The book catalog has also been published. Anyone wishing to obtain a copy only needs to pay the cost of seven cents and send it to Room 2, 5th Floor, No. 374 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, or P.O. Box 2064, and they will receive a copy, along with a complimentary copy of the [Ant] Library Special Publication published by the society.

The people are indeed falsely accused out of spite and did not go to rob together. Tao Rongquan testified that he used to work with Huang. He accused me of being a thief because I refused to give him clothing material, which caused him to harbor a grudge. Wang testified that he beat Huang because Huang harassed his widowed sister-in-law, causing him to harbor resentment and falsely accuse me of being a thief. I knew nothing about the robbery. The court, after verifying the testimonies, appointed a lawyer to defend Huang and then announced the end of the debate, scheduling the verdict for the 28th. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Nanyang Tobacco Company

Foreman Assault Case Opens

Postponed for Retrial

Zhang Desheng, a 44-year-old Shandong native and foreman of the curing department of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company at No. 269 Broadway Road, was known for his violent nature. Recently, he made unreasonable demands to the factory for a wage increase, and at 9:45 AM the previous morning, he gathered dozens of idlers, armed with tobacco knives, iron bars, and other weapons, and stormed into the tin packaging department on the third floor, wantonly destroying property and violently beating the department's staff members, Li Zhitang and Li Yongyao, who were seriously injured. At that time, carpenter Chen Ronggui stepped forward to stop them and was also injured. After someone reported to the Huishan Police Station, the police chief immediately dispatched Chinese Detective Zhang Ziqing, along with Chinese and foreign detectives, to apprehend them. They found Li and Chen Ronggui covered in blood, lying on the floor, unable to speak. They were taken by ambulance to the Baek Road Baolong and Haining Road Red Cross hospitals for treatment. Subsequently, Chinese and foreign detectives arrested Zhang Desheng, the leader of the assault, and took him into custody. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the case, stating that the victims, Li Zhitang, Li Yongyao, and Chen Ronggui, sustained serious injuries to their heads, chests, legs, and other parts of their bodies and were unable to attend the court. Witness Feng Haiquan from the company could identify everything. He requested a postponement of the trial. Lawyer Wu Linkun from the Nanyang Company attended the court to await instructions. Feng Haiquan testified that he was the director of the tin packaging department on the third floor of the company. The defendant was the foreman of the tobacco leaf room downstairs. At the time, he personally saw the suspect wielding a tobacco knife, smashing the doors and windows, and rushing in first, followed by fifty to sixty thugs, shouting to start the assault, saying that he would be responsible if anyone was killed. He then abandoned the knife and took an iron bar, repeatedly striking the two Li staff members to the ground and throwing teapots at them. Only then did carpenter Chen Ronggui step in to mediate and was also beaten down. When questioned, the defendant Zhang Desheng gave evasive answers. Judge Xiao Xiefei ordered that he be remanded in custody for a retrial.

155th Time

The 155th inspection report of the issuance reserve of the Central Bank stated: "According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of banknotes of this bank. On March 20, 22nd year of the Republic of China, Supervisor Qiaqing conducted the 155th inspection at the bank's Issuance Bureau. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of banknotes issued in silver dollars is 44,440,821 yuan, including 40,211,308 yuan in silver dollar notes and 4,229,513 yuan in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of reserve fund for banknotes is 44,440,821 yuan, including 36,961,821 yuan in cash reserve in silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 31,400,864 yuan stored in the bank's issuance vault, 3,689,321 yuan stored in branch offices in various ports, and 1,863,860 yuan deposited with fellow banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 7,479,000 yuan in silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold banknotes issued is 417,269.40 yuan. The total amount of reserve fund for customs gold banknotes is 417,269.40 yuan. This reserve fund includes 7,004.69 taels of standard gold, equivalent to 417,269.40 yuan in customs gold at a fixed price of 59.57. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's banknote regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guaranteed reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is made on March 20, 22nd year of the Republic of China, by the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank."

Reader Advisory

The Storm Aroused By Reading

A Message from Zhao Yongcheng from Our City

My home is located in a remote village surrounded by countless mountains. In that village, all feudal forces and old ethics are still fully preserved. In such a harsh environment, my younger sister was betrothed to the son of a local gentry by her parents through the words of a matchmaker when she was only six or seven years old. In the spring of 1920, the other party requested marriage. At this time, my younger sister was only sixteen years old and studying in the fifth grade of elementary school. Her fiancé was seventeen years old and also in the fifth grade of elementary school. Because both parties were too young, my family strongly opposed it. However, the other party's parents were too stubborn and repeatedly insisted, insisting on an immediate marriage. My family also insisted on opposing. Later, the other party said that the marriage was only a formality and that my younger sister would be allowed to continue her studies at home after the marriage. My parents were forced to compromise. However, my younger sister refused to comply and almost committed suicide. But how could a girl of only a dozen years old resist? In the end, she was forced to submit. Initially, the other party also agreed to allow my younger sister to return home to study. However, last spring, after my younger sister graduated from elementary school, she was determined to continue her studies in middle school. She sought the other party's opinion, but the other party absolutely opposed it, citing the inability to provide financial support. We repeatedly explained various reasons to the other party's parents, stating that we did not need any financial support and only asked for their permission. However, the other party remained stubborn and refused. My younger sister's desire to study was very strong and she was unwilling to submit. With no other choice, my younger sister and I resolutely decided to go to the provincial capital to take the entrance examination for the provincial girls' middle school. After being admitted, she enrolled in the school. A semester passed without incident. However, this spring, the other party demanded a divorce without giving any reason. In the past, both parties were very harmonious, with only some differences on the issue of education. My younger sister came to the province purely for the sake of studying and had absolutely no other intentions. She has also absolutely maintained the personality that girls should maintain in school. Now the other party suddenly demands a divorce. I respectfully request your guidance on how to resolve this problem and ask you to answer the following questions: (One)

The feelings between the couple have completely disappeared. If she does not divorce, my younger sister will inevitably be subjected to abuse. If peaceful methods cannot achieve harmony, what should we do to ensure my younger sister's future happiness? (Two) Based on the above facts, whose reasons are more sufficient in the eyes of the law? (Three) If the other party forces a divorce, how should we respond? Can we demand considerable compensation for youth and alimony after the divorce? What conditions and restrictions are there in the law? I respectfully await your reply.

Answer: According to your letter, your younger sister's differences with her husband's family are only due to the issue of education. Since the husband's family wants a divorce, if it is determined that they cannot live together for life, it is a good thing to take this opportunity to divorce. This is one thing. The reporter is not a legal expert. I dare not answer the second question hastily. But judging from reason and logic, if your younger sister is as you stated in your letter and there is nothing else that harms her character, then naturally the fault lies with the husband's family and not with your younger sister. Her reasons should be sufficient. This is two things. According to common sense, if the first party proposes a divorce, they must bear considerable alimony or compensation for loss of status to the second party; the same applies if the second party proposes a divorce to the first party. As for the specific legal provisions, there are lawyers to consult.

Page 12

Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn, a genre of essays)

Worrying for (Humor)

— Zhanlu

George Bernard Shaw's English pronunciation is Burner Shaw. If translated as (Baonai Xiao, 包倷笑, literally "guaranteed to make you laugh"), his humorous nature could be expressed through his name.

Ever since the old man (Baonai Xiao) came to Shanghai, then to Beiping, and then to Tokyo, the term humor has become almost universally known. However, I fear this is not to the benefit of humor! I am quite worried about the future of humor. Why am I worried about humor? Let me give you two reasons:

First, people in society who do not seek to understand thoroughly often interpret words literally and force themselves to understand things. In the past, the term (Romantic) was misunderstood as (having affairs), (stealing wives), (being promiscuous), (gambling wildly), and various other interpretations. Recently, (Modern) and (Model) have been forcibly interpreted as coquettish women and girls without pants. Following this pattern, the word humor, as it spreads in society, will certainly lose its true meaning. In the future, perhaps even now, some people will be discussing this word humor, saying, (Humor is the act of sitting silently in the dark.) Or, they might say, (Humor is a homophone of oiling/smearing.) From then on, misinformation will spread, and what will humor become? This is one aspect of my worry, worrying for the sake of humor itself.

Second, in our country, which is in a modern era of absolute freedom of speech? , does this environment allow us to imitate (Baonai Xiao) and his ilk and speak out boldly? The facts tell me that there have been quite a few people who have imitated that humorous (Baonai Xiao), and the result has only been (meeting their anger). While they were indulging in self-appreciation of humor, they were given a (Maybe it is humorous, 莫須幽) (Note) crime. When they were humorously (inviting the king into the urn 请君入瓮), wasn't laughing and crying both crimes, and humor was no longer humor? This is another aspect of my worry, worrying for the sake of those who imitate the old man of humor (Baonai Xiao).

(Note) "Maybe it is humorous" (莫須幽) is a homophone of "Maybe it is there" (莫须有), a term meaning "fabricated accusation."

□□□□

— A Wise Man

Selling Secrets

"□□□□" these few square blocks, are saying, because of the clash of Yin and Shen, the conflict of Chen and Xu, in the Republic of China year 22, it is due to have good luck in the annual cycle.

Square blocks, in small-scale newspapers in the mainland, are commonplace and not surprising. For example, if there is a familiar but unfamiliar character, the typesetting room happens not to have this lead type, so they frankly and without ceremony, ask the square block to act as the plenipotentiary representative.

In several large-scale newspapers in Shanghai, they sometimes play this game too. But under the square block, there is often a bracket attached, with the words "(telegraph code unknown)" in the middle, indicating that this is a helpless situation and does not require the reader's forgiveness.

But these days in the newspapers, the square blocks that are having good luck in their annual cycle, are neither due to a lack of lead type, nor due to an unknown telegraph code. Speaking of it, the source is big, but it was the Japanese who taught us this trick.

The fact is this: When the Songhu Anti-Japanese War broke out, Chinese newspapers very faithfully reported that a certain army was in a certain place, and a certain headquarters was in a certain direction. Damn it, no sooner had the newspaper been published than Japanese planes, as if they had eyes, flew to that certain place and certain direction to drop bombs.

At first, everyone didn't understand and only thought that the Japanese spies were very capable and had obtained the secrets. Later, a Japanese traitor said that with such news reporting, the Japanese army simply didn't need spies. They could just read the Chinese newspapers and follow the map, which was a great pleasure.

After suffering one loss, we learn one lesson, so these days, in the telegrams about the front-line war news, several square blocks are inserted, so that when the enemy sees them, although the dwarves have many lumps in their stomachs, they can't accurately guess what medicine is being sold in the gourd. What secrets are being sold in those square blocks?

On the first day of the month, the brigade, captured , killing thousand enemies, seizing countless, and is now advancing towards , expected to reach on the day, and can directly attack on the day.) Don't worry everyone, this is a Futurist reporter selling secrets.

From Aviation Sports to the Story of America

— Yun Lian

Worthy of Emulation

Shanghai, a large international trading port, after nearly a month of city-wide mobilization, after nearly a month of city-wide slogan shouting and propaganda for the cause of national salvation through aviation: according to newspaper reports, only a paltry sum of over ten thousand yuan was raised, of which ten thousand yuan was donated solely by the owner of Tianchu MSG Factory; this clearly tells the enemy that the city of Shanghai, which has the largest population in the country, and is known as the elite people standing on the forefront of the times, has only this much patriotic sentiment! A friend surnamed Li, when the European War broke out, was living in New York City. The United States was neither an Allied nor an Entente country; they only felt the tragedy of war! With the instinct of a love for peace and human mutual assistance, he convened a joint meeting of all public organizations in the city in one day to discuss organizing a battlefield work, such as a rescue team. He immediately asked: For example, for a part of the hospital, how much funding do you need in total? How much can you raise yourself? As a result, it was estimated that five million gold was needed. Over three days, the committee produced by the joint meeting investigated the annual profits of all the shops in the city clearly, and stipulated 10/50 of the profits to donate to this funding; after proper distribution, the joint meeting issued a notice that at 12 noon on a certain day, members of the association would knock on the doors and windows of your esteemed office with a form, and ask your executives to hand over the donation that should be paid to the person who comes; and then without delay, this surprising huge amount of donation was declared to be more than adequate.

An elderly merchant living with Mr. Li, who was a middle-class wealthy man, had already made a donation for another public cause because of his business profits, and according to the rules, he did not need to pay again; the old merchant was surprised that the joint meeting did not send anyone to collect the money, thinking that he had lost face, so he personally went to the joint meeting to ask, saying: "Doesn't my age qualify me as a citizen? Am I not qualified to love my country?" After the people in the association explained in detail, the old merchant returned home sullenly.

This story is a real event in New York City, not a fabricated tale! Compatriots, is our society so healthy? Should we emulate it? Or should we continue with the empty talk of national salvation through aviation?

Long Novel

Fourth Battalion Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 2: The Humble Abode Makes Friendly Neighbors, Secretly Admiring the Healthy Old Man, The Wealthy Family Chooses a Good Match, Scornfully Criticizing the Poor Girl

Old Zhao smiled and clasped his hands several times, saying, "I dare not accept this. I dare not accept this!" Mrs. Jiang smiled and said, "This is naturally a joke, how dare we be so presumptuous? In my humble opinion: it would be much easier if your battalion commander got married earlier. Having a young mistress at home is much better than having a daughter." Old Zhao said, "You are right, and that's why I let Ziqiang pick me up to live here. Alas, but when it comes to marrying a daughter-in-law, it is very difficult." As he spoke, he stroked his beard in a pensive manner. When people talk about betrothing girls and marrying daughters-in-law, the girl has no way to interrupt, so Guizhi only held a handful of melon seeds in her hands, chewing on them on the side, without speaking. Mrs. Jiang then asked, "I heard that the old man is from Baoding, is he in the city or in the countryside?" Old Zhao said, "We still have land to grow crops. The whole family lives in the countryside." Mrs. Jiang said, "There are probably many people in your family, right?" Old Zhao said, "There were three of us brothers, but now there is only one left. The younger generation is quite numerous, but they have all separated." Mrs. Jiang said, "How much land does your family have?" Old Zhao said, "Enough to eat and drink, about a hundred mu of land." At this point, Mrs. Jiang turned to Guizhi and said, "Listen, their family has a hundred mu of land." She then turned back to Old Zhao and said, "With so few people in your family, thirty or forty mu of land would be enough to live a good life. A hundred mu of land is more than enough." Guizhi finished eating all the melon seeds in her hand, picked up a cup of tea on the coffee table, and drank it. After finishing the tea, she hesitated for a while, put down the cup, and said to her mother, "Let's go back and hurry up with that dress. If we don't finish it by twelve o'clock, they will come to urge us again." Seeing her daughter's brows furrowed, perhaps because her daughter was unwilling to do this, Mrs. Jiang had no choice but to stand up and say goodbye to Old Zhao, smiling, "I've disturbed you again. Our house is dark and dirty, and I dare not invite the old man to come over and sit down. If the old man needs anything, just go over there to get it. We are all good neighbors." Old Zhao smiled and said, "My son and I have straightforward tempers. You don't see me being polite when I speak." Mrs. Jiang repeatedly said yes and returned home happily. (19)

Random Thoughts on Reading Newspapers

— Huo Xueming

Please Learn from Bu Shi's Patriotism

As usual, I read the newspaper every day, and glean some news about the northern war from under the big headlines. Perhaps I have not yet lost my sense of national identity, and I carefully savor the reports of our army's great victories with excited feelings. At this time, I simply laughed in my heart, ("Good fellows, a big saber waving towards the enemy's阵营, short Japanese guys fell down like shadows, satisfying! Is their army so useless!") I thought. So I opened my mouth, gesturing to people how to kill the enemy, and loudly praised the bravery of Song Zheyuan, Sun Dianying, and their subordinates. So I took out silver dollars and immediately sent them to the Volunteer Army Support Association to fulfill my personal responsibility as a commoner, and also to express my admiration. Whether we can (defend the Great Wall to the death) in the future, cannot be predicted now.

If you say that I took out the money, the purpose is to buy their glorious death, I am not a complete capitalist, I have not thought of this level. But those who harbor this kind of thought, in my opinion, are not necessarily non-existent. For example, after the news of Tang Yulin's abandonment of Chengde spread, some patriotic people who originally wanted to take out some money, refused to donate money to save the country at this time. ("Rehe has been lost, why donate money? To let the warlords deposit it in foreign banks!") They shouted in unison like this. Obviously, the reason why they donate money is to take the fact of victory as the price. Once disappointed, they think that the matter is over, and there is no need to use money anymore. They don't even need to save the country. But they have not thought that there are still soldiers resisting the Japanese in front of them, and there are still many national heroes going to the front line one after another. The rich who are unwilling to donate money because they are indignant at Tang Yulin's abandonment of his post and loss of land are mistaken. Even if Japanese soldiers have invaded the customs, and the government still says emptily (long-term resistance), but in fact takes no action; we should still save the country, those with strength should use their strength, those with talent should use their talent, and those with money should use their money. This meaning, even I know, carries a bit of nationalism, and is also close to shallow and ancient sayings, but in the current China, the way for the people to seek salvation on their own, it is still better to learn from Bu Shi of the Han Dynasty. As for the military in the front using knives to kill the enemy, it is a manifestation of strength: at the same time, it is also a manifestation of talent. Shouldn't we who are living in the rear stand idly by and watch? Can we save the country?

Biographical Sketches

Anecdotes of Weng Zhaoyuan

— Dingming

General Weng Zhaoyuan, who shook the East, all the women and children in the country can tell about his merits of defending Wusong for more than a month. Even those who have visited the battle sites, wandering around Paotai Bay and the Wenzaobang area, can't help but exclaim at General Weng's defense in the undefendable and his victory in the unachievable; however, there was a period of General Weng's life that was mostly overlooked by the world!

The fact is this: One day, I was working for the league, and suddenly found a package of things from August 16, 1930 in a pile of old papers. When I opened it, I was about to replace it with a new Shen Bao paper. Inadvertently, I saw a three-character headline: A Chinese student in France escapes danger and survives:) I suddenly thought that in the recent practice period of our country's flight comrades, I have repeatedly seen news of accidents; even foreign pilots have had facts of landing and dying. At the same time, I still inadvertently looked at two lines of small headlines: (Fell from five hundred meters with only minor injuries, the French press cites him as a brave Chinese.) My mood suddenly became tense after seeing it; these two headlines seemed to be spells that sucked me in, so I carefully read on:

(Paris Correspondence: Our student Weng Zhaoyuan (i.e. Weng Huiteng) graduated from the Japanese Army Academy last year, and then went to France to enter the Mo Guan Flying School, and has graduated from the second phase. Yesterday, when flying at five hundred meters, the engine suddenly failed, causing the fuselage to fall, breaking three high-voltage power lines, and the entire plane crashed. Weng was immediately sent to the Versailles Hospital by the army ambulance. Fortunately, the injuries were still minor, and he will be discharged from the hospital in a few days. This time, the plane fell from five hundred meters and broke the high-voltage power lines without being burned, which is also a strange thing. The French Aviation Department once sent people to study the cause of the fire. The French newspapers competed to say that it was lucky that he did not die. And praised him as a brave Chinese.)

(Oh! Weng, the brigade commander of the 156th Brigade, had such an anecdote!) After reading it, I felt this sentence from the bottom of my heart; and I got three feelings:

1. It is true that Weng had a strange experience to fall from five hundred meters and break the high-voltage power lines without being burned; and it seems that God deliberately teased him, leaving him to show his edge in the January 28th incident; but from the January 28th Weng took risks, and our army did not complete the work, it can also be seen (When Heaven is about to place a great responsibility on a man, it always first tests his resolution; exhausts his muscles and bones; frustrates his endeavors; and derails his undertakings, so that his mind is stimulated, his nature strengthened, and his abilities increased.) Mencius's words are absolutely correct! And poor boys should more resolutely harden their scalps and work hard, try!

2. The French newspapers competed to say that it was lucky that General Weng did not die, and praised him as a brave Chinese; then the Chinese people are inherently brave, and can be brave; the ancients said: (Heaven helps those who help themselves,) Oh, our Chinese people! Get up quickly! Get up quickly! Quickly be brave! Join the battle group, regard marching as child's play; regard airplanes and cannons as dragonflies flying and mantises waving their arms; regard the enemy army as poisonous bees, as bad guys, as evil horses, bravely cut them down, destroy them, and punish them, and permanently remove this thief for mankind! Now the athletes who join the flying world should be like General Weng, soaring in the sky, not afraid of dangers, forging flying skills, and promoting the spirit of fearlessness.

3. General Weng recently telegraphed on Yangri (7th) in Beiping to take over as the commander of the 117th Division. There are inspiring words in the text:

(Wrapped in horsehide, I have long cherished the heart of Fu Bo,

Burying bones in the sandy battlefield, I have long accumulated the ambition of Dingyuan.)

Seeing that (rectifying the army, inspiring the ten auras, driving out the jackals and tigers, and returning my rivers and mountains) is in front of us, this is the task of the Weng family. However, I especially hope that armed comrades with real strength will work together with one heart, unite, point their guns outward, sweep away the evil atmosphere, push away the haze; restore the glory of Changbai Mountain and Heilongjiang, and restore my glorious world.

News Headlines

Elementary School Students' Patriotism

Wang Zhaohong Goes to the Beijing Municipal Government

Please Issue Train Tickets to Go to Rehe to Kill the Enemy

(Nanjing, 21st) Wang Zhaohong, a 15-year-old elementary school student from Xujia Lane Elementary School in Beijing, brought a letter to the municipal government on the 21st to request to see Mayor Shi, requesting that he be issued a train ticket to Rehe so that he could go to the front line to kill the enemy. Shi was moved by his patriotism and, in addition to expressing his appreciation in person, sent him to the Social Affairs Bureau because he was young, and informed the school to take him back and persuade him.

Postponed to Double Tenth Festival

(Nanjing, 21st) The 2nd National Scout General Review and Jamboree, originally scheduled to be held in Beijing on May 5, is now postponed to the Double Tenth Festival due to insufficient preparation.

(Nanjing, 21st) The Ministry of Education approved the advice of the Training Directorate General and selected six methods for local garrisons to assist in national military education training, and issued orders to all departments and bureaus to forward them to public and private high schools and above for compliance.

(Nanjing, 21st) The Ministry of Education issued a total of 29 study abroad certificates in February, including one at public expense to England and 28 at private expense. Among them, one to England, two to the United States, two to Germany, eight to France, and fifteen to Japan.

The Ministry of Education instructed the Jiangsu Education Department regarding the explanation of the Education Association Law, stating that Article 8 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Education Association Law was set up for the convenience of members with two types of qualifications, so the choice of which district Education Association to join is entirely up to the individual and is not restricted. If a member of the Jia District Education Association feels inconvenient in the Yi District or other district education service, they may request to withdraw from the Jia District Education Association and join the Education Association of the service place.

Local

Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center

First Meeting of the Standing Council Yesterday

Office Opens at New Address on April 1

First Board Meeting in the Capital on the 9th

After the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center held its inaugural meeting at the Mausoleum Management Committee in the capital on the 12th of this month, the staff of the center immediately returned to Shanghai to handle the closing affairs of the preparatory committee, and temporarily borrowed Building 803 on Fuxu Road in the city as the address of the center in order to facilitate the collection of donors' funds and plan the initial work outline. After the donations have been collected in a certain amount and the work has been generally decided, bids will be invited for the construction of the building. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 p.m., the center convened its first meeting of the Standing Council at 10 Morrie Road. Those present were Sun Ke, Ye Gongchuo, Zheng Hongnian, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Yi-cheng, Li Zhaokun, and Shi Jingcai. Ma Chaojun and Li Dachao were present as observers. (Dai Chuanxian telegraphed that he was unable to attend due to other matters.) Sun Ke chaired the meeting and Li Dachao took the minutes. After the formalities were completed, the chairman first reported that the move to the new address would take place on April 1, and reported on the collection of the founders' start-up funds and the closing of the preparatory committee's expenses. Next, discussions began. 1. It was resolved that the center would open its office on April 1. 2. It was resolved that the initial work would be to organize a field survey map, focusing on land surveys, especially in bandit areas. 3. It was resolved to invite Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Wu Chaochu, Yang Duan-kan, Shi Liangcai, Wang Yunwu, Dai Chuanxian, Li Zhaosui, and Zheng Hongnian to be design committee members. 4. It was resolved to appoint Ye Gongchuo, a member of the Standing Council, to temporarily serve as the director of the secretariat, and Li Dachao to temporarily serve as the director of the administrative department. 5. It was resolved to elect Ye Gongchuo and Li Zhaosui as financial directors. 6. It was resolved that the center's budget would be implemented on a trial basis for three months according to the original proposal. 7. It was resolved that the start-up expenses would be temporarily set at 1,500 yuan. 8. It was resolved to ask Ye Gongchuo, a member of the Standing Council, to draft the detailed rules for operation and submit them for discussion at the next meeting. 9. It was decided that the first board meeting would be held at the Mausoleum Management Committee in Nanjing at 10:00 a.m. on April 9. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 p.m.

Regulations for Elementary, Secondary, Normal, and Vocational Schools (3)

Chapter 13 Guidance and Research

Article 94 Elementary school teachers shall participate in educational research organizations in their schools and localities, study the facts manifested in children's lives, and teaching methods.

Article 95 Elementary schools with five or more teachers shall organize educational research associations to study and improve school affairs and teaching and training matters. All teachers in the school shall be members, and meetings shall be held at least once a month, with the principal as the chairman.

Article 96 Elementary schools within a school district shall jointly organize elementary school education research associations in the district to study and improve elementary school education in the district. All elementary school teachers in the school district and the education committee members in the district shall be members, and meetings shall be held at least once every two months, with the principal of the elementary school in the district designated by the competent education administrative authority or a member of the education committee as the chairman.

Article 97 Elementary schools in a city or county directly under the Executive Yuan shall jointly organize city-wide or county-wide elementary school education research associations to study and improve elementary school education in the locality. Representatives of elementary schools in each school district designated by the competent education administrative authority shall be members, and meetings shall be held at least once every six months, with the chief education administrative officer or inspector of the city or county as the chairman.

Article 98 Elementary schools in five to seven counties and cities shall organize provincial regional elementary school education research associations to study and improve elementary school education in the provincial region. Representatives of elementary schools in each county and city designated by the Provincial Department of Education shall be members, and meetings shall be held at least once a year, with the principal of the provincial normal school or the affiliated elementary school or the provincial elementary school or the provincial inspector as the chairman.

Article 99 Elementary schools in the entire province shall organize the provincial elementary school education research association to study and improve elementary school education in the entire province. Representatives of the provincial regional elementary schools designated by the Provincial Department of Education and the directors, section chiefs, and inspectors of the Provincial Department of Education shall be members, and meetings shall be held at least once every two years, with the director of the Provincial Department of Education or his representative as the chairman.

Article 100 The Ministry of Education may convene representatives of elementary schools and primary education supervisors from all provinces and cities across the country to hold a national elementary school education research association to study and improve national primary education. The regulations will be separately determined when the research association is convened.

Article 101 Each province and city may designate a provincial elementary school or an affiliated elementary school of a provincial normal school in the provincial region as the central elementary school of the region, and the education administrative authorities of each city and county directly under the Executive Yuan may designate an elementary school in each school district as the central elementary school. The central elementary school in the preceding paragraph shall fully provide the results of the research to the elementary schools in the region or the school district for reference and implementation, but shall not mark the word "central" in the school name.

Article 102 Kindergarten teachers and education personnel related to elementary school education may participate in the research on elementary school education.

Article 103 Education administrative authorities at all levels shall be responsible for guiding various elementary school education research associations.

Article 104 The organizational regulations for elementary school education research associations below the provincial and municipal levels shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record.

Chapter 14 Supplementary Provisions

Article 105 These Regulations may be amended by the Ministry of Education when necessary.

Article 106 These Regulations shall come into force on August 1, 1933 of the Republic of China. (End of Elementary School Regulations)

(II) Secondary School Regulations

Chapter 1 General Principles

Article 1 These Regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Secondary School Law.

Article 2 Secondary schools are places for strictly training young people's minds and bodies and cultivating healthy citizens. In accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Secondary School Law, the following training shall be implemented:

1. Strengthening physical fitness, 2. Cultivating civic morality, 3. Nurturing national culture, 4. Enriching life knowledge and skills, 5. Cultivating a scientific foundation, 6. Developing labor habits, 7. Inspiring artistic interests.

Article 3 Secondary schools are divided into junior secondary schools and senior secondary schools. The length of study is three years each. A school that combines junior and senior secondary schools is called a secondary school, and a school that is set up separately is called a junior secondary school or a senior secondary school.

Article 4 The standard for the age of students in junior secondary schools is 12 to 15 years old, and the standard for the age of students in senior secondary schools is 15 to 18 years old.

Article 5 Public junior and senior secondary schools may separately establish simple normal courses and special normal courses.

Chapter 2: Establishment and Management

Article 6: The establishment, alteration, and cessation of provincial and municipal (referring to municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan) middle schools shall first be planned or justified by the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities and reported to the Ministry of Education for approval before implementation. The establishment, alteration, and cessation of county and joint county middle schools shall first be planned or justified by the competent education administrative authorities and reported to the provincial Department of Education for approval before implementation, and then reported to the Ministry for record. The establishment, alteration, and cessation of private middle schools shall be handled after being approved by the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities in accordance with the procedures stipulated in the regulations for private schools and then reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

The superior education administrative authorities may revoke the establishment, alteration, and cessation of public and private middle schools that are not handled in accordance with the procedures stipulated in the preceding paragraph.

The establishment and management of middle schools affiliated with public and private junior colleges or higher institutions shall be the same as those of public and private middle schools.

Article 7: Provincial middle schools shall be named after the place where they are located. County and municipal middle schools shall be directly referred to as "___ County/Municipal Middle School." If there are two or more public middle schools with the same name in one place, they may be distinguished by numerical order or by a smaller regional name as the school name. Joint county middle schools shall be called "___ Counties Joint County Middle School." Private middle schools shall use a specific name and shall not be directly named after a place name.

Article 8: Public junior high schools and senior high schools may be separately equipped with simplified normal courses and special normal courses only if they meet the following conditions:

1. The original middle school has completed all grades, and the teaching facilities are complete. 2. There is a definite need. 3. The funds are raised separately and are sufficient for handling. 4. Approved in advance by the competent education administrative authority.

Article 9: Public and private middle schools shall, within one month after the beginning of the first semester of each academic year, submit the following items to the competent education administrative authority for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record:

1. A list of new students, transfer students in each grade, returning students, students on leave of absence, dropouts, and students in each grade in the current academic year. 2. The academic qualifications, experience, positions, and salaries of the principal and faculty members in the current academic year, and whether they are full-time or part-time. 3. The budget for the current year. 4. Changes to the school rules, school buildings, and equipment for the current academic year. 5. Grade reports of students in each grade for the previous academic year. 6. The final accounts or income and expenditure items for the previous year.

Article 10: Public and private middle schools shall, within one month after the beginning of the second semester, submit the following items to the competent education administrative authority for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record: 1. A list of new students, transfer students in each grade, returning students, students on leave of absence, and dropouts in the current semester. 2. The academic qualifications, experience, positions, and salaries of newly appointed faculty members in the current semester, and whether they are full-time or part-time; the names of faculty members who have left office and the reasons for leaving office. 3. Grade reports of students in each grade for the previous semester.

Article 11: Public and private middle schools shall, two months before each graduation, prepare a resume of graduating students and grade reports for each year, and submit them directly or through the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities for approval before holding the graduation examination.

Article 12: Public and private middle schools shall, within one month after each graduation, prepare a graduation grade report of graduates and submit it directly or through the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 13: Provincial and municipal education administrative authorities shall dispatch supervisors to inspect and guide public and private middle schools at least once each semester, and submit the inspection and recommendations to the Ministry of Education for review within one month after the inspection is completed.

Chapter 3: Funding

Article 14: The start-up, regular, and temporary expenses of provincial and municipal middle schools shall be paid by the provincial and municipal funds. The funding for county or joint county middle schools shall be provided by the county or the counties involved in the joint establishment. The funding for private middle schools shall be provided by their boards of directors.

Article 15: County middle schools may receive provincial funding if they are genuinely located in poor areas and have excellent academic performance. Private middle schools shall not receive public funding unless they have truly excellent academic performance.

Article 16: The standards for public funding to county and private middle schools shall be stipulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities and reported to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 17: In the allocation of regular expenses for middle schools, salaries shall not exceed 70% at most, equipment expenses shall account for at least 20%, and office expenses shall not exceed 10% at most. The budget form shall be determined separately.

Article 18: The expenditure of middle school funds shall strive for thrift and accuracy, and the entire income and expenditure situation shall be subject to open and careful review by the financial audit committee. The review methods shall be formulated by the provincial and municipal education administrative authorities and reported to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Chapter 4: Organization

Article 19: Junior high school and senior high school students are divided into first grade, second grade, and third grade according to the curriculum progress.

Article 20: Each class shall have 50 students as a standard, but shall have at least 25 students.

Article 21: With the exception of physical education and military training, which may adopt other grouping methods for teaching, middle school subjects shall not be taught in combined classes.

Article 22: Middle schools shall, in principle, separate boys and girls into separate schools or separate classes.

Article 23: Newly established middle schools shall not enroll students above the second grade in the first year and shall not enroll students in the third grade in the second year.

Chapter 5: Curriculum

Article 24: The teaching subjects of junior high schools are civics, Chinese language, English, history, geography, mathematics, physics, chemistry, zoology, botany, physical education, hygiene, manual work, drawing, and music.

(Explanation)

1. The total number of hours of class and in-school self-study for junior high school students is 8 hours per day and 48 hours per week. The remaining time, in addition to class time, is in-school self-study time.

2. There must be teachers to supervise and guide during in-school self-study time.

3. All students, whether boarding or day students, must participate in in-school self-study.

4. Extracurricular activities and sports are not included in the in-school self-study time.

5. The time for in-school self-study and extracurricular activities and sports may be slightly adjusted depending on the region, season, and whether the students are boarding or day students.

2. The second foreign language refers to languages such as English, German, French, and Japanese.

3. Middle school junior high sections applying this curriculum shall first submit it through the competent education administrative authority to the Ministry of Education for approval and record.

4. If middle school junior high sections applying this table encounter special difficulties, they may reduce English by one or two hours per week, but they must submit it for approval to the competent education administrative authority for reporting to the Ministry of Education for record.

5. The total number of hours of class and in-school self-study for junior high school students is 8 hours per day and 48 hours per week. The remaining time, in addition to class time, is in-school self-study time.

9. In special circumstances, the Ministry of Education may be requested to approve the non-establishment of English courses and replace them with one type of second foreign language.

Article 25: The teaching subjects of senior high schools are civics, Chinese language, English, Chinese and foreign history, Chinese and foreign geography, mathematics, physics, chemistry, biology, physical education, hygiene, military training (military nursing for girls), logic, drawing, and music.

Municipal First

Public School Garden Closed for Visits

Internal Relocation of Botanical Garden

The Municipal Education Bureau Issued a Notice Yesterday

The Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that the number of visitors to the Municipal First Public School Garden is increasing daily, but the area is small and there is often a problem of overcrowding. In order to meet the needs of the citizens, the Bureau has already expanded the animal section of the garden and is building a new zoo at the original site of Qinpu on Wenmiao Road. The Botanical Garden has also been planned to be relocated, and the Municipal Government has approved the allocation of funds to build the Botanical Garden at the original site of Gezhi College on Longhua Road. All kinds of flowers and trees in the school garden need to be moved and transplanted urgently. It is hereby announced that visits will be suspended from this month onwards.

Baoshan

Agricultural Education Center Establishes Rural Improvement Association

Currently Being Reported to the Department of Education for Record

The Baoshan County Farmers' Education Center was completely destroyed internally due to the Japanese invasion of Shanghai. It was then ordered to be suspended by the Provincial Government, and the County Education Bureau sent personnel to take care of it. It is now learned that the center was ordered to be restored last month, and Ji Zhonghe was appointed as the director. After Mr. Ji took office, he actively reorganized the interior, which is now largely in order. From this semester onwards, he will focus on livelihood education. Recently, in addition to investigating specially contracted model farms, distributing seedlings, and promoting fish farming, he also invited nearby villagers to organize the Fuqiao Rural Improvement Association. All villagers in the district, regardless of gender, can join the association. Yesterday, the association held its inaugural meeting, attended by more than 100 farmers from 33 villages. Director Ji presided over the meeting and reported on the significance of establishing the association. The constitution was then passed, and Jiang Boying and 13 others were elected as committee members. The improvement matters are divided into rural autonomy, popular education, abundant livelihood, cooperative undertakings, and enhanced health. It is heard that the constitution is currently being submitted by the Education Bureau to the Provincial Department of Education for record, and the work of improving rural areas will begin.

Since its establishment, Binhai Middle School in this city has striven to develop its school affairs and improve its facilities.
